O Lion-God! I am Unbu, and I abhor the block of execution. Do not let my whole heart be torn from me by the divine champions in Heliopolis! O you who clothe Osiris and have seen Sutu, you who turn back after smiting him and have accomplished the overthrow, this whole heart of mine remains weeping over itself in the presence of Osiris. Its strength comes from him, obtained through prayer. I have been granted the glow of heart at the hour of the God of the Broad Face and have offered sacrificial cakes in Hermopolis. Do not let my whole heart be torn from me. I entrust its place to you and stir your whole hearts towards it in Sechit-hotepit and the years of triumph over all it abhors, taking all provisions at the appointed time from your hand. This whole heart of mine is laid upon the tablets of Tmu, who guides me to the caverns of Sutu and gives me back my whole heart, which has accomplished its desire in the presence of the divine Circle in the Netherworld. Let those who find the sacrificial joint and funereal raiment bury them.

Notes:
1. Unbu is a name of the solar God, associated with the hawthorn or another flowering bush. The term "golden Unbu" appears in the Pyramid Texts.
2. Divine champions are depicted with various determinatives, indicating different qualities.
3. The term "clothe" has multiple meanings, and the context usually determines the correct one. Some manuscripts provide additional determinatives for clarity.
4. The end of this chapter is considered unintelligible, with many variations in manuscripts. The text is likely corrupt, with scribes mixing different recensions without regard to grammatical sense.
5. Tablets or records are mentioned, with the term appearing in the Pyramid Texts in the sense of memory.
6. The last words of the chapter puzzled later scribes, who altered them in various ways. The older manuscripts refer to the sacrificial joint, not a verb as later scribes thought.

Chapter XXIX: Keeping the Heart in the Afterlife

Back, Messenger of your God! Are you here to take this whole heart of mine by force? But I will not surrender this heart of the living to you. The Gods regard my offerings and fall upon their faces on their own earth.

Notes:
The two oldest copies of this chapter are found on the coffins of Aniamu and Horhotep. The papyrus of Ani is the only early period text where it occurs. None of these texts is perfect, with parts missing or misplaced. Later scribes exercised their ingenuity, changing terms and adding negatives to make sense of the text.
1. The term "Messenger" is used here in the same sense as an angel or ambassador of God.
2. The term "by violence" appears in other religious texts.
3. "The Living" refers to those saved, in opposition to the dead and damned.

Chapter XXIX B: Another Chapter of the Heart; upon Carnelian

I am the Heron, the Soul of Ra, who conducts the Glorious ones to the Tuat. It is granted to their souls to come forth upon the Earth to do whatever their Genius wills. It is granted to the soul of the Osiris N to come forth upon the Earth to do whatever his Genius wills.

Note:
Certain chapters related to the heart were written on gems and served as amulets. This chapter was written on Carnelian and is not often found in papyri. M. Naville found copies in the Berlin Papyrus of Nechtuamen and another traced by Lepsius in Rome. A third copy is in the papyrus of Ani in the British Museum, with some variations.

Chapter XXX A: Keeping the Heart in the Afterlife

Heart mine, which is that of my Mother, Whole Heart mine, which was that of my coming upon Earth, let there be no estoppel against me through evidence; let no hindrance be made to me by the Divine Circle; let there not be a fall of the scale against me in the presence of the great God, Lord of Amenta. Hail to you, Heart mine; Hail to you, Whole Heart mine; Hail to you, Liver mine! Hail to you, Gods who are on the side lock, conspicuous by your scepters, announce my glory to Ra and convey it to Nehabkau. And though he be buried in the deep grave and bowed down to the region of annihilation, he is glorified there.

Chapter XXX B: Keeping the Heart in the Afterlife

Heart mine, which is that of my Mother, Whole Heart mine, which is that of my birth, let there be no estoppel against me through evidence; let no hindrance be made to me by the Divine Circle; do not fall against me in the presence of him who is at the Balance. You are my Genius, who is with me, the Artist who gives soundness to my heart.Chapter XXXI: Repelling Crocodiles in the Afterlife

Back off, Crocodile Sui! Do not come near me, for I live by the Words of Power. I speak the Name of the great God, who sends two of his Messengers: one named Batta and the other named "Your Aspect is Fixed Law." Heaven sets its time, and my Words of Power control everything related to it. My mouth speaks my Words of Power. I eat, and my teeth are like flint, my grinders like the Cliff of Tuf. You who watch over my Words of Power, do not take them away, O Crocodile who lives by your own Words of Power.

Notes:
1. The Words of Power are given to the deceased by Thoth in Chapter 23.
2. Some texts read "Do not you speak," implying the Crocodile might use the Words of Power.
3. The name Batta was later changed to the divine Ape Beni.
4. "Fixed Law" represents the central idea of regularity in the Book of the Dead.
5. "Determines" here means setting limits or defining.
6. "The Cliff of Tuf" refers to Anubis, often called "His Cliff."
7. "Sitting" is interpreted from various texts.

Chapter XXXII: Repelling Crocodiles in the Afterlife

Osiris stands up, supported by his Gods. O Son who speaks with your father, protect this Great one from these four crocodiles who devour the dead and live by the Words of Power. I know their names and ways, and I protect my father from them.

Back, Crocodile of the West, who lives on the Setting Stars. You have devoured Osiris's head, but I am Ra. Back, Crocodile of the East, who lives on those who consume their own filth. I have come, and I am Osiris. Back, Crocodile of the South, who lives on impurities. Let not the red flame be upon you, for I am Septu. Back, Crocodile of the North, who lives on what lies between the hours. Let not your fiery water harm me, for I am Tmu.

All things that exist are in my grasp, and those that are not yet depend on me. I am equipped with your Words of Power, O Ra, with what is above and below me. I have gained length, depth, and fullness of breath within my father's domain. He has given me the beautiful Amenta, where the living are destroyed but its possessor remains strong. My face is unveiled, and my heart is in its place. The Uraeus is upon me daily. I am Ra, who protects himself, and no evil can overthrow me.

Notes:
1. The chapter is in poor condition, with few early manuscripts available.
2. The ancient text mentioned only four crocodiles, but later texts mention eight.
3. The myth suggests that stars setting are swallowed by the Crocodile of the West.
4. Instead of Ra, later texts mention Sut.
5. "Septu" is a name found in various texts.Chapter XXXIII: Keeping Serpents Away

Stop, serpent Rerek! Seb and Shu are here. If you don't, you'll eat the rat Ra despises and gnaw the bones of a rotten cat.

Notes:
1. This chapter is often found in coffins. A similar chapter is in Horhotep's tomb, mentioning Rerek and Shu but not the rat and cat. These animals symbolize the impurities the damned face in the afterlife.

Chapter XXXIV: Avoiding the Shrine Dweller

O Urgeus! I am the Flame that shines and opens eternity, the column of Tenpua with blossoming plants. Stay away! I am the Lynx Goddess.

Notes:
1. The meaning of "Urgeus" is unclear. The text has many variations, and the scribes often altered it.
2. "Open out Eternity" is the oldest and most accepted reading.
3. Tenpua is likely a misreading. The text suggests another deity, but it's uncertain.
4. The Lynx Goddess, Maftit, represents swift speed and is mentioned in other chapters as fighting the dragon of darkness.

Chapter XXXV: Avoiding Serpents in the Underworld

Oh Shu, here is Tattu, under Hathor's wig. They scent Osiris. The serpent Seksek passes over me. Here are bruised wormwood and reeds. Osiris prays to be buried. The Great One's eyes are downcast, cleansing and balancing the issues.

Notes:
1. "Wig" refers to the Gods' head-dress, symbolizing light clouds at sunrise or sunset.
2. "Scent" can also mean nursing or putting to sleep.
3. The early texts are inconsistent and hard to translate.
4. "Bruised" can mean either guard or beat down.
5. "Cleansing" is generally understood as washing.
6. "Balancing the issues" refers to the circumstances of one's life.

Chapter XXXVI: Keeping the Apshait Away

Stay away, you with parted lips! I am Chnemu, the Lord of Shennu, bringing the Gods' words to Ra and announcing the news to Nebes.

Notes:
1. The Apshait is likely a voracious insect, not a tortoise as previously thought. The last word of the chapter is uncertain, with variations in different texts.

Chapter XXXVII: Keeping the Merta Goddesses Away

Hail, Merta Goddesses! I inform you of my Words of Power. I rise from the Sektit boat. I am Horus, son of Isis, here to see my father, Osiris.

Notes:
1. Merta signifies two eyes, representing Isis and Nephthys.

Chapter XXXVIII: Living by the Breath of Air in the Netherworld

I am the God in Lion form, heir of Ra and Tmu in Chemnis, the Master in their halls. Those in their cells guide me. I travel the heavenly Ocean on Ra's Bark, uttering his words to the living and the breathless. I spy for Ra at sunset, compressing my mouth and feeding on life. I live in Tattu, repeating my life after death like the Sun daily.

Notes:
1. There are two versions of this chapter. The one translated here is the canonical version found in later manuscripts.
2. Chemnis is where Isis gave birth to Horus.Chapter XXXIX: Repelling the Serpent Rekrek in the Underworld

Back off, stabber from Apepi! Drown in the lake of Heaven, where your father ordered your demise. Stay away from this birthplace of Pa, the God surrounded by his terrors. I am Ra, surrounded by his terrors. Back off, dark demon, and the sword you wield! Ra casts down your words; the Gods twist your face; the Lynx Goddess tears out your heart; the Scorpion Goddess chains you; and Maat deals the final blow. The Gods on the roads overthrow you. Apep, the enemy of Ra, falls.

You who remove the bolt from the East of Heaven at the stormy voice of bellowings, and open the gates of the Horizon before Ra: he comes forth fainting from the wounds. I am a doer of your will, O Ra. I have done well, to your satisfaction. I raise shouts of acclamation at your success in fettering Apep. Apep is fallen and in bonds. The Gods of the South, North, West, and East bind him; their bonds are upon him. Aker overthrows him, and the lord of the ruddy sky binds him. Ra is satisfied; Ra makes his progress peacefully. Apep falls; Apep goes down, the enemy of Ra.

Be emasculated, O Apep, enemy of Ra; be repulsed whom Ra hates; look behind you: a chopper is over your head to divide it into two parts, and those above your head assail it. Your bones are broken, your limbs are severed under Aker's direction, O Apep, enemy of Ra. Your boatmen, O Ra, succeed in measuring out your path, and a journey with which you are satisfied; a progress towards home; and the progress you have made towards home is fair. Let no evil hindrances come forth against me from your mouth in what you do towards me. I am Sutu, who causes storms and tempests, and who goes round the Horizon of Heaven, like one whose heart is veiled.

Tmu says: Let your countenances be raised up, soldiers of Ra, and drive back Nebtu in the presence of the Divine Circle. Seb says: establish those who are upon their thrones in the middle of the Bark of Chepera; seize your shields and spears, and hold them in your hands. Hathor says: Seize your daggers. Nut says: Come and drive back Nebtu, who comes against him who dwells in his shrine, and makes his voyage in solitary guise: the Inviolate God, the resistless one. O Gods in your Divine cycles, who travel round the lake of Emerald, come and defend the Great one who is in the shrine from which all the Divine cycle proceeds. Let glory be ascribed to him, and let honor be given to him. Oh then, proclaim him with me.

Nut says, the mother of the Gods: He comes forth and finds his path, and makes captures of the Gods; he has the first place in the two houses of Nut. Seb stands still, the great cycle of the Gods is in terror, Hathor is under terror, and Ra is triumphant over Apep.

Notes:
1. The text is extremely uncertain, making any translation conjectural.
2. Aker: The God Aker is imagined as a tunnel starting from where the sun sets and extending through the earth to where the sun rises. Each end of the tunnel has a sphinx-like form, with a human-headed lion at both the entrance and the terminus. The solar bark enters on the Western horizon and comes out on the Eastern.
3. The proof: The term "taste" is used metaphorically to mean a probe or test. In Egyptian texts, a hero's hand is said to "taste" his enemy, similar to the Homeric concept of tasting one's enemy in battle.

Chapter XL: Repelling the Eater of the Ass

Back, serpent Haiu, whom Osiris curses. May Thoth cut off your head, and may I gain whatever property comes from you as decreed by the Gods for your slaughter. Back, you whom Osiris curses, from the Neshemet galley, which sails south with a favorable breeze. Pure are you, all Gods who overthrow the enemy of Osiris. The Gods on the larboard side shout loudly. Back, Eater of the Ass, whom the God Chas in the Tuat curses. Know me! (Repeated four times).

"Who are you?" I am "Down upon your face!" you who eat at my sanctuary. I am the Season, which comes at its own will. "Come not against me; you who come uncalled and unknown." I am the master of your utterance and the check on your pride. O Ha-as, whose horns Horus cuts: by my children, the cycle of Gods in Pu and Tepit, you are severed from your fold and your fold is severed from you. And he who cuts you off comes forth as the Eye of Horus; you are kept back and stopped by the breath of my speech.

O God who devours all wrong and carries off with violence; there is no wrong in me, my tablets are free from wrong. Let me not suffer violence before the Divine Circle; let not disaster be hurled upon me. I am he who gives or takes according to your behest. Let not iV be seized, let him not be devoured. He is Possessor of Life and Sovereign Lord on the Horizon.

Notes:
1. The translation is based on the important papyrus T 5 of Leyden, known as Lb, the only manuscript containing the whole chapter.
2. The Eater of the Ass is a serpent, but the "Ass" symbolizes something specific, not the animal itself.Chapter XL: Repelling the Eater of the Ass

Back off, serpent Haiu, cursed by Osiris. May Thoth cut off your head, and may I gain whatever is decreed by the Gods from your defeat. Back off, you who Osiris curses, from the Neshemet galley, which sails south with a favorable breeze. Pure are you, all Gods who overthrow Osiris's enemy. The Gods on the larboard side shout loudly. Back off, Eater of the Ass, cursed by the God Chas in the Tuat. Know me! (Repeated four times).

"Who are you?" I am "Down upon your face!" you who eat at my sanctuary. I am the Season, which comes at its own will. "Come not against me; you who come uncalled and unknown." I am the master of your utterance and the check on your pride. O Ha-as, whose horns Horus cuts: by my children, the cycle of Gods in Pu and Tepit, you are severed from your fold and your fold is severed from you. And he who cuts you off comes forth as the Eye of Horus; you are kept back and stopped by the breath of my speech.

O God who devours all wrong and carries off with violence; there is no wrong in me, my tablets are free from wrong. Let me not suffer violence before the Divine Circle; let not disaster be hurled upon me. I am he who gives or takes according to your behest. Let not iV be seized, let him not be devoured. He is Possessor of Life and Sovereign Lord on the Horizon.

Notes:
1. The translation is based on the important papyrus T 5 of Leyden, known as Lb, the only manuscript containing the whole chapter.
2. The Eater of the Ass is a serpent, but the "Ass" symbolizes something specific, not the animal itself.

Chapter XLI: Avoiding Slaughter in the Netherworld

O Tmu, let me be glorified in the presence of the God in Lion form, the great God; that he may open to me the gate of Seb. I prostrate myself to the great God who is in the Netherworld. Let me be introduced into the presence of the company of Gods who preside over those in Amenta. O you who are at the gate of Tebat; God with the Red Crown, who is in Amenta; let me feed, let me live by the breath of air and accompany the great Cleaver and the Bark of Chepera. Let me speak to the divine Boatman at the gloaming, let me enter in and let me go out; that I may see who is there; that I may raise him up and speak my words to him. O Breathless one: Let me live and be saved after death. O Bearer of peace offerings, who opens your mouth for the presentation of the tablets, for the acceptance of the offerings and for the establishment of Maat upon her throne; let the tablets be brought forward, and let the Goddess be firmly established. I am Osiris, the great God, the eternal king, who numbers his seasons and who lifted up his right arm, who judges the great ones and gives mission to the Gods of the great Circle which is in the Netherworld.

Notes:
1. The most noteworthy difference between the older recension of this chapter and that of the Saitic and later periods is that in the latter the God addressed at the opening is Osiris Unneferu, who is identified with Tmu. In the older recensions, the identification may be seen in another way. Tmu is the God invoked, and in answer, he says that he is Osiris, the great God.
2. God with the Red Crown is one of the titles of Osiris with the crown. This title, derived from the crown, is Net-td or Nait-td. It was borne by the high priest at Coptos, and the King of Egypt derived his title from the Crown of the North which he wore as representing Osiris, or rather the heir of Osiris, Horus.
3. The great Cleaver, the name of the God who cleaves his path through the sky.
4. Breathless one, Osiris.
5. Thoth is the person here addressed, and the speaker is Osiris. The tablets are those containing the evidence at the trial at the Balance.
6. Acceptation, besides the physical sense of comprehendere, 'to lay hold of with the hands,' has that of 'taking in, embracing with the mind,' and perhaps 'setting forth in words.'
7. On the Sarcophagus of Seti, and the other copies of the same text, there is a picture of these Gods. The text speaks of them as the Gods of the great Circle.

Chapter XLII: Preventing Slaughter at Sutenhenen

Land of the Rod, of the White Crown of the Image, and the Pedestal of the Gods. I am the Babe. (Said Four Times.) O Serpent Abur! You say this day, "The Block of Execution is furnished with what you know," and you come to soil the Mighty One. But I am he whose honors are abiding. I am the Link, the God within the Tamarisk, who connects the Solar orb with Yesterday. (Four Times.) I am Ra, whose honors are abiding. I am the Link, the God within the Tamarisk.

My course is the course of Ra, and the course of Ra is my course. My hair is that of Nu, my two eyes are those of Hathor, my two ears those of Apuat, my nose that of Chenti-chas, my two lips those of Anubis, my teeth those of Selkit, my neck that of Isis, the Mighty, my two hands those of the Soul most Mighty, Lord of Tattu, my shoulders those of Neith, Mistress of Sais, my back is that of Sut, my phallus that of Osiris, my liver is that of the Lords of Cher-abat, my knees those of the most Mighty one, my belly and my back are those of Sechit, my hinder parts are those of the Eye of Horus, my legs and thighs those of Nut, my feet those of Ptah, my nails and bones those of the Living Uraei. There is not a limb in me which is without a God. And Thoth is a protection to my flesh. I shall not be grasped by my arms or seized by my hands. Not men or Gods, or the glorified ones or the damned; not generations past, present, or future, shall inflict any injury upon me. I am he who comes forth and proceeds, and whose name is unknown to man. I am Yesterday, "Witness of Eternity" is my Name: the persistent traveler upon the heavenly highways which I survey. I am the Everlasting one. I am felt and thought of as Chepera. I am the Crowned one. I am the Dweller in the Eye and in the Egg. It is an attribute of mine that I live within them. I am the Dweller in the Eye, even in its closing. I am that by which it is supported. I come forth and I rise up: I enter and I have life. I am the Dweller in the Eye; my seat is upon my throne, and I sit conspicuously upon it. I am Horus, who steps onwards through Eternity.

I have instituted the throne of which I am the master. As regards my mouth: whether in speech or in silence, I am right and fair. As regards my attributes: I hasten headlong, I the God Unen, with all that pertains to me, hour proceeding from hour, the One proceeding from the One, in my course. I am the Dweller in the Eye; no evil or calamitous things befall me. It is I who open the gates of Heaven; it is I who am master of the throne, and who open the series of births upon this day. I am the Babe, who treads his path of Yesterday. I am "This Day" to generation of men after generation. I am he who gives you stability for eternity, whether you are in heaven or upon earth; in the South or in the North, in the West or in the East, and the fear of me is upon you. I am he who fashions with his eye, and who does not die a second time. A moment of mine belongs to you, but my attributes belong to my own domain. I am the Unknown one, but the Gods of Ruddy Countenance belong to me. I am the Gladsome one, and no time has been found, but served to create for me the Heaven and the increase of Earth, and the increase of their offspring. They sever and join not; they sever my name from all evil things, according to the words which I say unto you. It is I who rise up and shine forth; strength proceeding from strength, the One proceeding from the One. There is not a day devoid of that which belongs to it; forever and forever. I am Unbu, who proceeds from Nu, and my mother is Nut. O you who have set me in motion! for I was motionless, a mighty link within the close of Yesterday; my present activity is a link within the close of my hand.I am Horus, the eternal prince, a flame that ignites your hearts towards me. I am the master of my throne, moving forward. The present is the path I have cleared, freeing myself from all evil. I am the golden Cynocephalus, three palms high, without limbs, in the Temple of Ptah. My journey mirrors that of the golden Cynocephalus. Let these words be spoken: Ababak ter-ek.

Notes:
This chapter is crucial for understanding Egyptian mythology. The speaker identifies with the Sun God, representing the eternal Sun of Yesterday, Today, and Forever, "One proceeding from the One."

1. Sutenhenen: Later texts refer to this as the "Netherworld."
2. The Babe: A term for the rising Sun, symbolizing something "lifted up."
3. Serpent Ab-ur: A viper known for causing intense thirst, possibly due to its habit of waiting by water sources.
4. To soil: An earlier term replaced in later texts.
5. The Link: A title for the Sun God, symbolizing connection and order.
6. The God within the Tamarisk: The rising Sun often depicted in a tree or bush, symbolizing the light cloud or mist at dawn.
7. Who connecteth: Likely refers to a rope or bond, symbolizing connection.
8. Identification of limbs: The deceased's body parts are associated with various Gods, a common theme in Egyptian texts.
9. Strength: Literally a wall or tower.
10. Continuously: Repeated for emphasis.
11. The interjection implies addressing a second person.
12. Recent copies mention the Sanctuary of Ptah at Memphis.
13. Ababa-k ter-ek: A formula with various interpretations.

CHAPTER XLIII: Ensuring one's head is not severed in the Netherworld
I am a Prince, the son of a Prince; a Flame, the Son of a Flame, whose head is restored after being cut off. Osiris's head is not taken, and neither will mine. I rise, renew, and grow young again. I am Osiris.

CHAPTER XLIV: Preventing a second death
Let the Cavern of Putrata be opened for me, where the dead fall into darkness, but the Eye of Horus supports me, and Apuat raises me up. I hide among the Stars that never set. My front is Ra, my face revealed by Thoth's words; my heart and speech are intact. I am Ra, not to be ignored or molested. Your father lives for you, O Son of Nut! I am your son Horus, seeing your mysteries and crowned as King of the Gods. I do not die a second time in the Netherworld.

CHAPTER XLV: Escaping corruption in the Netherworld
Here is Osiris, motionless like Osiris; let his limbs not remain motionless or corrupt. They move not, they stir not: let it be done for me as for Osiris. I am Osiris.

CHAPTER XLVI: Ensuring the living are not destroyed in the Netherworld
Oh, recent offspring of Shu, who dawn after dawn possesses his diadem at sunrise; future generations of men, my emergence is that of Osiris.

Note: This chapter addresses the offspring of Shu, who are future generations of men, not yet lived on earth. They circle the Sun before appearing on earth, and the glorified dead converse with them. The Egyptians believed in the preexistence of souls as part of their traditional creed.

CHAPTER XLVII: Ensuring one's seat is not taken in the Netherworld
Chair and Throne of mine, coming to me and circling around me; divine ones!

I am a noble Sahu, grant that I may follow the great God. I am the Son of Maat, and I abhor wrong. I am the Victorious one.

Note: Sahu is not a mummy but a living personality in mummified form.

CHAPTERS XLVIII and XLIX are identical to X and XI respectively.

CHAPTER L: Avoiding the divine Block of Execution
The four fastenings of the back of my head are secured. He in heaven made them firm for the fainting one on the day the fleece was shorn. Sutu and the Gods secured the fastenings in his first triumph. Let there be no disaster. Preserve me from him who slew my father. I am seized.### Chapter LI: Avoiding Falling in the Netherworld

I reject it, I reject it, I do not consume it. What I reject is filth. I do not eat it to appease my spirit. Let me not fall into it; let me not touch it with my hands, let me not step on it with my sandals.

**Note:** Chapters 51 and 52 are not found in the oldest papyri, but their essence and formulas appear on ancient coffins and in the Pyramid texts. Contrary to some interpretations, these texts do not suggest that the deceased will only have excremental matter to eat and drink in the afterlife. Instead, they express the Sun-God's abhorrence of such matter, as he is a consuming fire that devours everything in his path.

### Chapter LII: Avoiding Eating Filth in the Netherworld

I reject it, I reject it, I do not consume it. What I reject is filth. I do not eat it to appease my spirit. Let it not fall upon me; let me not touch it with my hands, let me not step on it with my sandals. Let me live on corn in your presence, Gods, and let someone bring me the seven loaves for Horus and the loaves for Thoth. "What will you eat?" the Gods ask. Let me eat under the Sycamore of Hathor the Sovereign, and let my turn be given among those who rest there. Let me manage the fields in Tattu and prosper in Heliopolis. Let me eat the bread of white corn and drink the beer of red barley. Let the forms of my father and mother be granted to me, the gatekeepers of the stream. Let the path be made clear for me, and let me sit wherever I desire.

**Notes:**
1. The later texts often contain errors, such as misreading certain words.
2. The term "corn" should be corrected from unintelligible forms in later texts.
3. The forms of the deceased's parents are mentioned in the Turin Book of the Dead and other texts.

### Chapter LIIIa: Avoiding Eating Filth or Drinking Lye

I am the sharp-horned Bull, who regulates the sky, the Lord of the risings in heaven; the great Giver of Light, who emerges from Flame; the Bond of Time, richly supplied with years; the God in Lion form, to whom is given a march of Glory. I reject it, I reject it, I do not consume what my spirit rejects. Let it not enter my stomach, let it not touch my hands, let me not step on it with my sandals. Let me not drink lye, let me not advance headlong in the Netherworld. I possess bread in Heliopolis, bread in Heaven with Ra, and bread on earth with Seb. The Sektit boat has brought it from the house of the great God in Heliopolis. I am gladdened in my very entrails and am associated with the divine mariners who circle to the East of Heaven. I eat as they eat, and I feed on what they feed. I eat bread from the house of the Lord of offerings.

### Chapter LIIIb: Avoiding Eating Filth

I reject it, I reject it! I do not consume it. Filth is what I reject; I do not eat it. I reject lye, I do not drink it. Let me not touch it with my fingers, let me not step on it with my sandals. Seb, the father of Osiris, has ordained that I should not eat filth or drink lye, but my father has four times said that I should eat of the red corn. There are seven loaves in Heaven at Heliopolis with Ra, seven loaves on earth with Seb, and seven loaves with Osiris. The God of the Sektit galley and the Maatit galley has brought them to me at Heliopolis. I shout with joy, and my spirit shouts with joy because I am in Heliopolis, living in excellent condition before Ra, on the day when bread is presented in Heliopolis.

**Note:** Chapter 53A is from older papyri, while 53B is an even older text from the Coffin of Horhotep.

### Chapter LIV: Receiving Air in the Netherworld

I am the God in Lion form, the Egg in the Great Cackler, and I watch over that great Egg which Seb has separated from the earth; my Life is the Life thereof, and the same is true of my advance in life and my breathing of the air. I am the God who maintains balance as his Egg circles around. For me dawns the moment of the most mighty one, Sut. O Gods who are pleasant through the alternate successions of the Earth, who preside over sustenance and live in the Blue, watch over him who abides in his Nest; the Infant God who comes forth towards you.

**Notes:**
1. The text followed here is from Pa, which is preferable to that of Ani.
2. The God in Lion form is not mentioned in Horhotep, where the chapter begins differently.
3. The egg springs from the back of Seb, not from the earth.
4. The equilibrium of forces is maintained by the revolution of the Sun.
5. The Blue refers to lapis lazuli, a term that has different connotations in ancient and modern contexts.### Chapter LV: Another Chapter for Receiving Air

I am the Jackal of jackals, I am Shu, who brings breezes to the Glorious One, reaching the ends of the sky, the earth, and the filaments of clouds. I provide air to the young ones as I open my mouth and gaze with my two eyes.

**Notes:**
1. The "Glorious One" is often read as Ra.
2. "Filaments of clouds" refer to the long, fibrous forms of cirrus clouds.

### Chapter LVI: Another Chapter of Breathing

Oh Tmu, give me that refreshing air from your nostrils. I hold the great station in the heart of Heracleopolis. I watch over the egg of the Great Cackler, my strength is its strength, my life is its life, and my breath is its breath.

### Chapter LVII: Breathing Air and Commanding Water in the Netherworld

Let the Great One be opened to Osiris; let the two folding doors of Kabhu be thrown wide to Ra. O great Coverer of Heaven, in your name of Stretcher of Heaven, grant me command of water, just as Sut commands force on the night of the Great Disaster. Let me prevail over those who preside at the Inundation, just as the venerable God prevails over them, whose name they do not know. May I prevail over them. My nostril is opened in Tattu, and I rest in Heliopolis, my dwelling, built by the Goddess Seshait and raised by Chnum.

If the sky is at the North, I sit at the South; if the sky is at the South, I sit at the North; if the sky is at the West, I sit at the East; and if the sky is at the East, I sit at the West. By raising my eyebrows, I pierce through to any place I desire.

**Notes:**
1. The Great One refers to Heaven.
2. Kabhu is another name for the Sky.
3. The Coverer refers to both the Nile and the Sky.
4. Stretcher may also mean "Cleaver of the Sky."
5. Force, like the Latin "vis," may not necessarily be criminal.
6. The Goddess Seshait is often misnamed as Safkh.
7. Raising eyebrows signifies scornful pride.

### Chapter LVIII: Breathing Air and Commanding Water

Let the door be opened to me! Who are you? What is your name? I am one of you! Who is with you? It is the Merta. Turn away then, face to face, upon entering the Meskat. He grants that I may sail to the Abode of those who have found their faces. Collector of Souls is the name of my Bark, Bristler of Hair is the name of the Oars, Point is the name of its Hatch, Right and Straight the name of the Rudder. The picture of it represents my glorious journey upon the Canal. Give me jars of milk, cakes, and meat at the House of Anubis. If this chapter is known, he enters after having gone out.

**Notes:**
1. Merta refers to the Goddess pair Isis and Nephthys.
2. Meskat or Meschenit is another reading.

### Chapter LIX: Breathing Air and Commanding Water

Oh Sycomore of Nut, give me the water and wind within you. I hold the abode in Heracleopolis, I watch over the Egg of the Great Cackler. My strength is its strength, my life is its life, and my breath is its breath.

**Notes:**
1. The mythological tree in heaven produces both wind and water, akin to the rain-cloud.

### Chapter LX: Another Chapter

Let the doors of Heaven be open to me, let the doors of Kabhu be thrown wide to me; by Thoth and Hapi, the great Coverer of Heaven, at daybreak. Grant me command of water, just as the mighty Sut commanded his enemies on the Day of Disaster to the Earth. May I prevail over the Long-armed ones in their corners, just as the glorious and ready God prevails over them, whose name they do not know. May I prevail over the Long-armed ones.

### Chapter LXI: Another Chapter

I am he who proceeds from the Weeper, whose attribute is Overflowing. I have command of it as Hapu.

**Notes:**
1. The great Weeper is primarily Heaven.
2. The Nile God also bears the same name.

### Chapter LXII: Drinking Water in the Netherworld

Let the Great One be opened to Osiris; let the Kabhu be thrown wide to Thoth, the Coverer, Lord of the Horizon, in his name of the Divider of the Earth. May I have command of the water, just as the might of Sutu had over his enemies. I traverse the Heaven: I am Ra, the God in Lion form, the Steer. I eat the haunch and pierce through the joint. I go around the Sechit-Aarru. Eternity without end is assigned to me. I am the Heir of Endless Time, and my attribute is Eternity.

**Notes:**
1. The Steer is a solar title frequent in the Pyramid texts.

### Chapter LXIIIa: Not Burned by Fire, Drinking Water in the Netherworld

O Bull of Amenta, let me be borne to you! I am the Rudder of Ra, conveying the Ancient ones. I am not burned, I am not consumed. I am Babai, the eldest son of Osiris, who strikes the eye of every God in Heliopolis. I am the Heir, the primary power of motion and rest.

### Chapter LXIIIb: Not Boiled in Water

I am the ready Rudder wherewith Ra conveys the Ancient ones, raising the effluxes of Osiris to the Tank from impassable flames; a wrecked one, but not to be consumed. I lie helpless as a dead person and arrive at the lair of the Lion who defies slaughter, following the road by which I set out.

**Notes:**
1. Chapters 63A and 63B are often combined in later manuscripts.### Chapter LXIV: Emerging from the Netherworld

I am Yesterday, Today, and Tomorrow, reborn again and again. I possess the unseen Force that creates the Gods and provides sustenance to those in the Tuat, the western realm of Heaven. I am the Eastern Rudder, the Lord of Two Faces, who sees by his own light. I am the Lord of Resurrections, emerging from the dusk, born from the House of Death.

Oh divine Hawks on your gables, who attentively watch over the matter, you who accompany the bier to the tomb and guide Ra's ship from the highest place in the Ark of Heaven, the Lord of the Shrine in the Earth's centerI am He, and He is I. My radiance is the light in which Ptah floats over his firmament.

Oh Ra, who smiles cheerfully and whose heart delights in the perfect order of this day as you enter Heaven and rise in the East, the Ancients and those who have gone before acclaim you. Make your paths pleasant for me; widen your ways for me to traverse the earth and the expanse of Heaven. Shine upon me, oh gracious Power, as I approach the divine words my ears shall hear in the Tuat. Let no pollution from my mother be upon me; deliver and protect me from him who closes his eyes at twilight and ends in darkness.

I am the Overflower, and Kam-ura is my name. I bring to fullness the hidden Force within me. Oh Great One, who is Shoreless and calls upon the Powers of the South when the God is carried forth, saying: "Behold the Lord of his Flood; see, the Shoulder is fastened upon his neck and the Haunch upon the head of the West," offerings which the two Goddesses of the West present to me when the weeping bursts forth from me at what I witness, as I am borne around on the Tenait in Abydos, and the bolts on the gateways above your images are within your reach.

Your face is like that of a hound whose nostril sniffs at the covert to which my feet convey me. Anubis is my bearer, for he who lulls me to rest is the God in Lion form. Save me! I am He who comes forth as one who breaks through the door; everlasting is the Daylight created by his will.

"I know the deep waters" is my name. I satisfy the desires of the Glorified, who are by millions and hundreds of thousands. I am the guardian of their interests, actively working at the hours of the day and adjusting the arms of Sahu; twelve in circling round, uniting hands, each with another. The sixth of them in the Tuat is the 'Hour of the overthrow of the Sebau,' which comes here in triumph; the same which makes way into the Tuat; the same which is yoked with Shu.

I shine forth as the Lord of Life and the glorious order of this day: the blood which purifies and the vigorous sword-strokes by which the Earth is unified. I sever the horns from those who unite in resistance to me; the hidden ones who rise up in opposition against me; those who go upon their bellies. I come as the ambassador of the Lord of lords to avenge the cause of Osiris in this place. Let not the Eye consume its tears. I am the Guide of the house of Him who dwells in his treasures. I come from Sechem to Heliopolis to inform the Bennu of the matters of the Tuat.

Oh Goddess Aucherit, who conceals what is within you but raises up forms like Chepera, grant that I may come forth and see the orb of the sun, and walk forth in the presence of the great God, who is Shu and abides for eternity. I travel on high, I tread upon the firmament, I raise a flame with the daylight which my eye has made, and I fly forward towards the splendors of the Glorified in the presence of Ra daily, giving life to every man who treads on the lands upon the earth.

Oh you who leap forth, conductor of the Shades and Glorified ones from the Earth, let the fair path to the Tuat be granted to me, made for those in faint condition and for the restoration of those in pain. Who are you, who devours in Amenta? I am He who presides in Restau. "He who enters in his own name, and comes forth in quest; the Lord of the Eternity of the Earth" is my name. She who has conceived has set down her burden; which turns round before descending; the door is shut at the wall which is reversed.

His Eye has been given to Horus and his face brightens at the dawning of the day. I am not exhausted: I become the Lion God and the palm flowers of Shu are upon me. I am not one who drowns. Blessed are they who see the Bourne; beautiful is the God of the motionless heart who causes the stay of the Overflowing. Behold! there comes forth the Lord of Life, Osiris your support, who abides day after day. I embrace the Sycomore, I am united to the Sycomore. I part the two deities of morning that I may come to hold the Eye, and cause it to rest in its place.

I come to see Ra at his setting, and I unite with the breeze at his coming forth: my two hands are pure for adoring him. May I be restored! May I be restored! I fly up to heaven and alight upon the earth; and my eye turns back towards the traces of my footsteps. I am the offspring of Yesterday; the tunnels of the earth have given me birth, and I am revealed at my appointed time. May I be sheltered from the warlike-handed God who comes behind me, may my flesh be sound and my glories protect the limbs of one who waits to take counsel. May the Cycle of the Gods listen to what I say.

To be said on coming forth by day; that one may not be kept back on the path of the Tuat, whether on entering or coming forth; for taking all the forms one desires; and that the soul of the person does not die a second time. If this chapter is known, the person is made triumphant upon earth and in the Netherworld, performing all things done by the living. This chapter was discovered on a plinth of the God of the Hermu Bark by a master builder of the wall in the time of King Septa, the Victorious. This composition is a secret; not to be seen or looked at. Recite the chapter when sanctified and pure; not approaching women, not eating goat's flesh or fish.

**Notes:**
1. This is one of the most important and ancient chapters. The text was already doubtful at the time of the XIth dynasty. It had been handed down in two recensions, both inscribed on the coffin of Queen Mentuhotep. The discovery of one of these is attributed to the time of King Septa of the 1st dynasty, and the second to the time of Menkaura, the king of the third pyramid. These two recensions are also found in the papyrus of Nebseni. The manuscripts present numerous variations, few of which are of significant value. These have been collected in various museums and analyzed in a work by M. Paul Guieysse, who translated and commented on them.The papyrus of Nebseni has been published, and M. Naville has documented all the variations found in the few existing papyri from the best period. I have notes on the readings of the papyri in the British Museum, and also from a cast (now in the British Museum) taken from a serpentine block belonging to the Hermitage Museum in St. Petersburg. Using these diverse sources, I have tried to present the chapter in as clear a form as possible, based on the texts in the papyrus of Nebseni and the rubric attributing the discovery to the time of King Septa. Some passages remain untranslatable due to text corruption. M. de Rouge read his translation of this chapter before the Acadmie des Sciences years before his untimely death, but it was never published. I also have a version by Mr. Goodwin, with whom I studied this and other chapters nearly thirty years ago. However, this type of literature was not where his remarkable insight shone.

When reading this and almost every other chapter of the Book of the Dead, it's crucial to remember that different divine names do not necessarily imply different personalities. A name represents just one attribute of a person or thing, and one person with several attributes may have several names. This chapter does not imply that the Sun is the Nile or the Inundation, but that the same invisible force manifested in solar phenomena also produces the inundation; He is the Inundator. But he has many other names and titles. In this chapter, as in others, the speaker sometimes identifies with a deity and at other times speaks as a mortal seeking favor.

1. The term "one whose force is concealed or unseen" is a theological term used throughout Egyptian religion, indicating that the deity should not be confused with its external manifestation. The Sun we see hides as much as it reveals the Sun-God, who has other manifestations.

2. Those in the Tuat are called "the Gods of the West" in more recent texts.

3. The divine Hawks on your gables represent the two divisions, North and South, of the kingdom of Horus.

4. The Shrine in the center of the Earth is also mentioned in the 'Book of Hades.'

5. "He is I, and I am He" is a concept found in the Pyramid Texts, indicating a unity between the deity and the individual.

6. Ptah floats over his firmament, as shown in early texts.

7. The adjective "gracious Power" is also written with a hieratic form.

8. Kam-urii, "The great Extender," is a name for Osiris, as the Nile.

9. The yearly inundation is the mature result of the innate force of the God.

10. The term "shoreless" implies an enclosed space with fixed limits, but the inundation has no determinate banks.

11. The usual sacrificial joints, shoulder and haunch, are mentioned.

12. The two Goddesses of the West, Isis and Nephthys, are also deities of the East or Sunrise.

13. The Tenait in Abydos is a feast commemorating the death of Osiris, his mutilation, mummification, and burial.

14. The bolts made fast on the gateways are invoked in the Pyramid Texts on behalf of the deceased.

15. "He who lulls me" refers to the double lion.

16. "I sever the horns" is similar to a passage in Psalm 75:11.

17. The term "lands" varies in the texts and can mean locality, post, or spot of earth.

18. "Blessed are they who see" is written in the Pyramid Texts.

19. The Sycamore of Dawn is repeatedly mentioned in the Book of the Dead and the Pyramid Texts.

20. To hold the Eye, later texts have different verbs synonymous with embracing, holding, enclosing, fastening, staying, or propping.

21. The God of the Hennu Bark resides in the ship referred to in Chapter I. The God of this ship is commonly named Sekaru in the texts, but Hennu is also one of the names of Horus.

22. King Septa of the 1st dynasty, identified with Usaphais of Manetho, is associated with the discovery of this chapter. The second recension describes the discovery at Hermopolis on a slab of alabaster.Prince Hortataf discovered a blue-inscribed slab under Osiris' feet during King Menkard's reign. He took it in the royal chariot after seeing its inscriptions. The text suggests placing a scarab of hard stone, purified with gold, on the deceased's heart, and reciting the 30th chapter's "Heart mine of my mother" incantation. Gold leaf has been found on some scarabs but is mostly missing now. The 'Ritual of Parma' mentions using two metals, gold and silver, for the scarab, which should be placed at the deceased's throat. It was the 30th chapter, not the 64th, that Prince Hortataf discovered.

**Chapter 65: Emerging Victorious by Day**
"Oh, you who shine from the Moon, let me emerge and be revealed in glory. Open the Tuat for me. Let me live and bring my adversaries in bonds before the divine Circle. May my mother's spirit be appeased as I rise with a golden scepter and sever limbs. May I rise as a Babe from between the knees of Sothis."

**Notes:**
- This chapter is similar to Chapter 2 but is not found in older papyri. M. Naville published a version found in five ancient papyri, though they are corrupt and unintelligible in parts. The oldest form is from the papyrus of Nebseni, which is the shortest and shows signs of interpolation. M. Naville used the text of Ca for collation.

**Chapter 66: Emerging by Day**
"I know I was conceived by Sechit and born of Neith. I am Horus, from the Eye of Horus. I am Uat'it, soaring like a Hawk on Ra's brow at the prow of his Bark in Heaven."

**Chapter 67: Opening the Doors of the Tuat**
"Open the doors of Nu's caverns and free the feet of those in glory. Let Shu's caverns open so I may emerge from my funereal pit to my seat at Ra's Bark's prow, without disaster."

**Chapter 68: Emerging by Day**
"Open Heaven's and Earth's doors for me. Let Seb's bolts open and the First Mansion be revealed. Let me pass into the Re-hunit and possess my heart, mouth, limbs, and funereal meals. Let me have air, water, the stream, the river, and the banks. Let me have all things ritually offered in the Netherworld. Let me sit under palm trees in Heliopolis with Hathor, as the solar orb broadens. Let me possess my heart, mouth, limbs, and funereal meals. Let me be raised up and strain for the breeze like a skilled pilot. If this scripture is known, he will travel the earth uninjured forever."

**Notes:**
- Copies of this chapter are found on coffins in Berlin and published by Lepsius. They are in poor condition, so the translation follows Theban papyri.
- The Re-hunit is a passage between the Netherworld and heaven or earth.
- The passage explains the "God of the Broad Face" in Chapter 28. Hathor proceeds to Heliopolis with divine writings.
- The superstition of "whistling for a breeze" among sailors is recognized here.

**Chapter 69: The Flaming One**
"I am a Flaming One, brother to a Flaming One. I am Osiris, brother to Isis. My son Horus avenges me with his mother against my adversaries. Chains bind their arms, hands, and feet for their evil deeds. I am Osiris, eldest of the Gods, heir of Seb. I am Osiris, Lord of life, powerful before and behind. My phallus extends to humanity's limits. I am Sahu, assigning bounds as I sail the starry throng of Heaven, my mother Nut's body. I am Anubis on the day of Rending asunder. I am the Bull in the Field, Osiris, who shut up his parents on the day of great slaughter. My father is Seb, my mother is Nut. I am Horus, eldest of Ra. I am Anubis on the day of Rending asunder. I am Osiris. O great One, who speaks to the guardian of Osiris' door, grant me entry and glory. Let me be appraised and made vigorous to avenge myself. Let me sit at Osiris' cradle, ending my suffering and pain. Let me be strong and renewed with Osiris. Said twice. Let me seize the Thigh under Osiris' place to open the Gods' mouths and sit by him like Thoth the Scribe, with offerings of loaves, beer, beef, and fowl. I offer to Horus, present to Thoth, and sacrifice to the Lord of Heaven."

**Chapter 70: Another Chapter**
"I have come to an end for the Lord of Heaven. I am sound of heart, resting at Osiris' table, King of Tattu, and my heart is stirred by his count."**Chapter 71: Emerging by Day**

"O Divine Hawk, who rises in Heaven, Lord of Mehurit, make me whole as you have made yourself whole. You reveal yourself, disrobe, and present yourself to the Earth. May the Lord of the One Face fulfill his will towards me. I am the Hawk in the Tabernacle, piercing through the Veil. Here is Horus, the Son of Isis. Make me whole as you have made yourself whole. May the Lord of the One Face fulfill his will towards me. I am the Hawk in the Southern Heaven and Thoth in the Northern Heaven, calming the Flame and conveying Law to the God who loves it. Here is Thoth. Make me whole as you have made yourself whole. May the Lord of the One Face fulfill his will towards me. I am Unbu of En-areref, the Flower of the Abode of Occultation. Here is Osiris. Make me whole as you have made yourself whole. May the Lord of the One Face fulfill his will towards me. O you who stand on your two legs, at your own hour, owner of the Two Twin Souls, and who live in Two Twin Souls. Make me whole as you have made yourself whole. May the Lord of the One Face fulfill his will towards me. O you who circle within your Egg, Lord of Mehurit. Make me whole as you have made yourself whole. May the Lord of the One Face fulfill his will towards me. Sebak stands erect, surrounded by his high places, and Neith stands erect in her alluvial grounds, revealing themselves, disrobing, and presenting themselves to the Earth. May the Lord of the One Face fulfill his will towards me. 

Oh, you Seven Divine Masters, who are the arms of the Balance on the Night when the Eye is fixed; you who strike off heads and cleave necks, who seize hearts and drag forth whole hearts, and accomplish the slaughter in the Tank of Flame: you whom I know and whose names I know, know me as I know your names. I advance to you, advance to me: live in me and let me live in you. Convey to me the Symbol of Life and the Sceptre you grasp. Award me the life of yearly speech through countless years, months, days, and nights, so I may come forth and beam upon my own images, with breath for my nostrils, and eyes that see, amid those at the Horizon, on the day when brute Force is brought to reckoning. If this Chapter is known, there is well-being on earth with Ra and a fair abode with Osiris, and the person is glorified in the Netherworld. They are granted sacred cakes and the coming forth into the presence each day, undeviatingly, for times infinite."

**Notes:**
1. The title is taken from the oldest known manuscript, that of Nebseni. The Papyrus Pe, of the same period, has "Chapter for entering after going forth by day, and for making transformations in all forms." The most recent form is in the Turin copy: "Chapter for coming forth by day and repelling brute Force, so that the person may not be seized in the Netherworld, but that their soul may be made sound in the Ta-t'eserit."
2. Lord of Mehurit = Lord of Heaven, the Sun-God. The invocation is repeated: "O you who circle within your Egg, Lord of Mehurit." The God is also said to be the owner of "the Two Twin Souls," Ra and Osiris.
3. The verb is in the second person, not the first, as shown by texts that give the person's name instead of the pronominal suffix.
4. "Thyself" uses the third person pronoun, following a known Egyptian idiom.
5. Lord of the One Face = the Sun, in contrast to the Moon, which has many phases. The God is also called the "Lord of Two Faces" at the beginning of chapter 64, representing the bright and dark aspects.
6. This passage is illustrated by the great inscription of Pianchi, who visited the great Tabernacle of the Sun-God at Heliopolis, lifting the Veil and performing rituals. The Hebrew Holy of Holies was similarly separated by a curtain with Cherubim figures, with an altar for incense offerings.
7. The Seven Divine Masters were the offspring of Mehurit, taking the form of Hawks. They were patrons of arts and sciences, assisting Thoth in composition and earth measurement. They are identified with the seven stars of the Great Bear, with Thoth representing the Polar star.
8. The Symbol of Life and the Sceptre.
9. Brute Force, see chapter 57, note 5.

**Chapter 72: Emerging by Day and Passing through the Ammehit**

"Hail to you, Lords of Rule, devoid of Wrong, living forever, whose secular period is Eternity. I make my way towards you. Let me be glorified through my attributes; let me prevail through my Words of Power, and let me be rated according to my merit. Deliver me from the Crocodile of this Land of Rule. Let me have a mouth to speak, and let my offerings be placed before you; because I know you, and I know your names: and I know the name of that great God to whose nostrils you present delicacies: Tekmu is his name. Whether he makes his way from the Eastern Horizon of Heaven or alights at the Western Horizon of Heaven, let his departure be my departure, and his progress be my progress. Let me not be stopped at the Meskat; let not the Sebau have mastery over me; let me not be repulsed at your gates, let not your doors be closed against me; for I have bread in Pu and beer in Tepu. And let me join in..."I bring my hands together in the sacred place my father Tmu has given me. He has established a home for me above the earth, filled with endless wheat and barley, which my own son offers to me during festivals. Grant me the funeral offerings of beef, fowl, bindings, incense, oil, and all good and pure things that sustain a deity, regularly and eternally, in any form I desire.

Let me descend or ascend to Sechit-aarru and arrive in Sechit-hotep. I am the God in Lion form. If this book is learned on earth or written on the coffin, the person will come forth by day in any form they wish, entering their house without hindrance. They will receive bread, beer, and meat on Osiris's table. They will come forth to Sechit-aarru and be given wheat and barley, flourishing as if they were on earth, doing as they please like the Gods there, forever.

Notes:
1. Ammehit is a name for the sixth abode in Amenta, but here it refers to the Netherworld.
2. Lords of Rule: This term can refer to spirits who have passed trials or Gods who have never been mortal, all possessing a "ka" (spirit).
3. The secular period of the Gods is eternity.
4. The Crocodile may refer to the monster in the Psychostasia (weighing of the heart) scenes.
5. Bread: The Egyptian word "ta" means something pierced or perforated, similar to sacrificial cakes in Leviticus.

Chapter 74: Moving on Earth
Do what you must, O Sekaru, as the God in his house and the God standing on his legs in the Netherworld. I shine above the Leg constellation as I come forth in Heaven, but I lie helpless with a corpse-like face. I faint as I advance, before the teeth of those who raven in the Netherworld.

Note:
1. The Leg constellation is in the northern sky, identified with Cassiopeia. It never sets below the horizon and is associated with purification.

Chapter 75: Coming to Heliopolis
I have come out of the Tuat, from the ends of the Earth, lighting up the Tank. I pass through the noble dwellings of the coffined. I open the dwelling of Remrem and reach the house of Achsesef. I enter the house of Kemkem. The Tet amulet places its hands on me and assigns me to its sister and mother, Kehkehit, who sets me on the Eastern path of Heaven where Ra rises daily. May I arise and be led on, assuming the mummied form as a God, traveling the path of Thoth as he appeases the two Combatants (Sut and Horus).

Notes:
1. Achsesef is a master of those in Amenta.
2. The Tet amulet has its own chapter (156) and is often depicted with hands and feet.
3. The two Combatants are Sut and Horus.

Chapter 76: Assuming Any Form
I have entered the Royal Palace, brought by the Bird-Fly. Hail to you who fly to Heaven, lighting the stars and protecting the White Crown. Make a path for me to follow.

Note:
1. The Bird-Fly is identified with the mantis and is the Tiller of the Rudder of Osiris's ship.

Chapter 77: Becoming the Golden Hawk
I transform into the Golden Hawk, emerging from its Egg. I fly and hover as a Hawk with a four-cubit wingspan, my wings made of green gem. I come forth from the Sektit Bark and rise from the Eastern Hill. I stoop upon the Atit Bark to raise those in their circles who bow to me.I present myself as the magnificent Golden Hawk with the head of a Heron, whose words Ra listens to every day. I sit among the great Gods of Heaven. The fields and their produce are before me; I eat and become radiant, fully satisfied. Nepra has restored my throat, and I possess everything that belongs to me.

Notes:
1. This chapter is the first in a series about "Transformations," which are not like the Greek or Indian concept of Metempsychosis. In Egyptian belief, changing form is a matter of will and glorification, not punishment for sin. The forms taken by the deceased in the Book of the Dead are well-known forms of the Sun-God.
2. The "green gem of the South" likely refers to emeralds, as noted by Pliny and other sources.
3. Nepra is another name for Osiris, associated with the giving of corn.

Chapter 78: Becoming the Sacred Hawk
Oh Horus, come to Tattu, clear my paths, and help me navigate my dwelling places. Look upon me, exalt me, and instill in me Terror and Might, so the Gods of the Tuat fear me and their defenses work in my favor. Protect me from the God who hides his name and those who might harm me in the house of darkness.

Oh Gods who listen to divine words, hush and hear what a God says to another God in a case of Divine Law. Osiris, grant me the transformation you have spoken of, so I may see your attributes and powers. Let me come forth and master my two feet, standing firm like the Inviolate One on high. May the Gods of the Tuat fear me and their defenses work for me. Let me run with your Punners but remain steadfast like the Lord of Life. Unite me with Isis the Mighty, protecting me from harm.

I seek words from Seb and sustenance from the Inviolate One on high, so the Gods of the Tuat fear me and their defenses work for me. I am one of the Bright ones in Glory, with attributes like those who come forth to Tattu. I am invested with the Soul of the one who speaks on my behalf. Instill in me Terror and Might, so the Gods of the Tuat fear me and their defenses work for me.

I am the Bright one in Glory, created by Tmu, originating from the apple of his eye. He has glorified and honored those with him. He is the Unique in Heaven, praised as he emerges from the Horizon, feared by Gods and glorified ones. I am one of the beings created by the eye of the Lord of Oneness. Before Isis gave birth to Horus, I grew and was honored among those in Glory.

I arose as the Sacred Hawk, invested with Horus's Soul to claim his inheritance from Osiris in the Tuat. The God in Lion form, presiding over the House of the Nemmes, told me to return to the confines of Heaven, as I am invested with Horus's attributes. The Nemmes is not for me, but I have free utterance to the confines of Heaven.

I claimed Horus's inheritance from Osiris in the Tuat, and Horus repeated to me what Osiris had said on his Burial Day. The God in Lion form gave me the Nemmes so I could advance to Heaven, seen by those on the Horizon, feared by the Gods of the Tuat, and supported by their defenses.

At the divine words, all at the funereal shrine of the Lord of Oneness bow low. The God in Lion form gave me the Nemmes and wings, granting me strength through his might, so I do not fall upon Shu. I appease my fair brother, the Master of the two Uraei. I know the paths of Heaven, its breezes upon me, and I am not stopped by the raging Bull as I navigate the Field of Eternity, guiding myself through the darkness and suffering of Osiris's deceased ones.

I come daily through the house of the God in Lion form, passing to the house of Isis the Mighty, to see glorious, mysterious, and hidden matters. I am invested with Horus's soul, seeing what is within it, and when I speak at the Doors of Shu, they respond immediately. I oversee the inheritance of Horus from Osiris in the Tuat. I am Horus in Glory, master of his diadem and Light, advancing to the Goal of Heaven. Horus is on his seat and throne. My face and back are that of the Sacred Hawk, equipped as his master.

I come forth to Tattu to see Osiris, bowing before him and Nut. They and the Gods see me, the Eye of Horus and the Flame in the Two Eyes. They reach out to me, and I stand firm against evil. They open the bright paths for me, seeing my attributes and listening to my words. Hail to you, Gods of the Tuat, with repellent faces and aggressive fronts, guiding the Stars and making the bright paths of the Hematit for the Lord of the Soul Most Mighty. Horus has ordained that you lift your faces and look upon me.

I display myself as the Sacred Hawk, invested with Horus's soul to claim his inheritance from Osiris in the Tuat. I bypass the long-haired Gods and those in charge of their dens, reaching those who preside over their caverns and the House of Osiris. I speak to them, making them recognize the God of Mighty Terrors, armed with horns against Sutu. They grant me a gracious pass, recognizing my divine provisions and powers of Tmu.

I make the paths bright in the Horizon and the Hematit in Heaven, firming the defenses for Osiris. I follow the command to come forth to Tattu, see Osiris, and report on the fortunes of his beloved son who pierced Sutu's heart. I recount the divine plans Horus executed in Osiris's absence. O Lord of the Soul Most Mighty, raise me up to see the Tuat. May all paths in Heaven and on earth be open to me, with no repulse.

Osiris, you are exalted on your throne, your hearing is good, your back strong, your head firmly fastened, your heart glad, confident in the strength and courage of those around you. You are established as the Bull of Amenta. Your son Horus sits on your throne, ruling over all life. Endless generations serve and fear him, as do the Gods. Tmu, the Sole Force of the Gods, has decreed it so.

Horus is the offering and the altar, reconstituting and restoring his father. He is the father, mother, brother, and kinsman, proceeding from his father's essence and overcoming his corruption. He rules over Egypt, with the Gods in his service, giving life to endless generations with his Eye.This chapter is rarely found in its complete form, as seen in the Turin Todtenbuch. The shortest version is in the tomb of Horhotep, containing only a few lines but providing the earliest form of the invocation formula. The common reading adds a pronoun suffix to both the verb and its subject, which is ungrammatical. The papyri Ati, Fg, and Ij correctly omit the suffix after the verb in the early part of the chapter. The coffin of Amamu has a chapter with the same title but a different text.

The Sacred Hawk and the Golden Hawk are distinguished only by color, indicating age rather than kind. The typical Egyptian Hawk can be identified with the Falco Lanarius or the Peregrinus. Naturalists say the Lanier of Buffon is the mature male Peregrinus, and the Lanner of Pennant is a young female Peregrine.

The term "baiu" refers to powers. The word "fi" seems connected to motion and corresponds to the Greek "balbis" or the Latin "carceres," the starting and goal posts. The symbol "Q" represents investiture, and a mummified person is called "invested."

The "apple of the eye" literally means point or thorn. The Nemmes is the royal head-dress, mentioned only in this chapter of the Book of the Dead but also in other religious texts. Different manuscripts introduce divine names, but the text is often unsatisfactory. The scribe of Pg ends the chapter with "I am the great God."

The portals of Shu, representing Daylight, respond to the God who comes as Horus. The term "Hetnatit" refers to a place near the Horizon, mentioned only in this chapter. Some divine names are unknown to the copyists and written at random.

Chapter LXXIX: This chapter allows one to assume the form of the Chief God of the Divine Cycle. Tmu, Lord of Heaven, gives motion to all things and creates life. He is self-produced and gives vigor to men. The Gods of the divine circuit and Amenta are addressed, seeking purification, strength, and power. Offerings of perfume, incense, and natron are made to stop the Gods' anger. The speaker claims to know the Gods' names and attributes, appearing as a God in human form, exalted like Ra, and receiving offerings.

Chapter LXXX: This chapter allows one to assume the form of the God who gives Light to the Darkness. The speaker completes the vesture of Nu, lighting up the darkness and uniting with the two brother-Gods. They raise the fallen one and balance Sutu in the mansions above. The speaker equips Thoth with light and seizes the Crown, embodying Maat. They lighten the darkness and overthrow devouring monsters, worshipped by those in darkness.

Chapter LXXXI: This chapter allows one to assume the form of the Lotus. The speaker is the pure Lotus from Ra's nostril, journeying for Horus. The text is difficult, with copyists differing on the interpretation.

Chapter LXXXII: This chapter allows one to assume the form of Ptah, eating bread, drinking beer, and sitting among the great Gods. The speaker flies like a Hawk, alights on the Aat, and execrates dirt. They live on offerings, enjoy bread and beer, and sit under Hathor's date trees. The speaker's head is Ra's, and they are summed up as Tmu, recording Tmu's words and inspiring fear. They are declared the heir of Seb, purified, and given Theophanies. The dwellers in Annu bow to them, and they are more powerful than the Lord of Time.

Chapter LXXXIII: This chapter allows one to assume the form of the Bennu bird. The speaker wheels and turns, flourishing like a flower and hiding like the Hider. They are the Barley corn of every God and the four Yesterdays of the seven Uraeus deities born in Amenta. Horus gives light through his body, opposing Sutu with Thoth in between.Chapter LXXXIV: Transforming into the Heron Hawk

You who hold the bound victims, with knives over their heads and locks and fleeces; you aged and bright ones armed with fate. I ascend to heaven but strike upon the earth, and vice versa. My power brings victory and raises the heavens, and I purify the earth beneath my feet against sinful cities, cutting down those in rebellion. I leave the Gods on their paths but strike the Wakers in their coffins. I do not know Nu, Tatunen, or the Red ones when they oppose me. I do not listen to a Word of Power. I am the Red Calf on the tablets. The Gods say, "Let your faces be unrestrained towards him who comes to me." The morning dawns independently of you; you do not control them. My alternations are in my own hands. I do not say wrong instead of right. Day after day, my eyebrow turns back unswervingly. Evening begins my voyage to celebrate the Reclining and the Embrace of the Aged one who oversees the Earth.

Chapter LXXXV: Transforming into a Soul

This chapter helps one avoid the dungeon. Imperishable is he who knows it. I am a Soul. I am Ra, who comes from Nu, and my soul is divine. I produce food but reject what is wrong. I possess Maat and live by it. I am the Food that does not perish, in my name of the Self-originating Force, along with Nu, in the name of Chepera, from whom I am born daily. I am the Lord of Daylight and reject Death. Let me not enter the dungeons of the Gods of the Tuat. I give glory to Osiris and appease the hearts of those with him, my friends. They fear me and show my might to those in their domains. Behold me, raised upon my pedestal and throne. I am Nu. Wrongdoers will not overthrow me. My orbits are ancient; my soul is divine, the Eternal Force. I create the Darkness at the edges of Heaven. My Soul, advanced in age, creates Darkness at Heaven's edges at my will. I reach the limits and advance on my feet. I lead and traverse the steel firmament, which acts as a curtain. I stop the Darkness and worms; my name is hidden. I drive away aggression from the Lord of the two hands, who is my own Soul. The Uraeus divinities are my body. My image is Eternal, the Lord of years, the King of Everlasting. I am exalted as Lord of the land of Rebu: 'the Youth in Town, the Lad in the Country' is my name; my name is imperishable. I am the Force that creates Heaven and resides in the Netherworld. My nest is unseen; my Egg is unbreakable. I am the Lord on High. I have made my nest at Heaven's edges and descend to Seb's earth to stop evil. I see my father, the Lord of the Gloaming, and breathe.

Chapter LXXXVI: Transforming into the Swallow

I am the Swallow; I am the Swallow. I am the Scorpion-bird, daughter of Ra. O Gods, whose perfume is delightful: Flame from the Horizon: O you in the place where I brought the keeper of his fold - let me have your arm to observe at the Tank of Flame, to advance as an envoy and report. Open it to me so I can tell what I have seen. Horus commands his bark. He has been given his father's throne, and Sutu, Nut's son, is under the grappling hooks he made. I have discovered what is in Sechera. I have touched Osiris's Heart with my hands. I have come to report what I found. Let me enter and report my mission. I purify myself at the great stream where my ills cease, and my wrongs are pardoned, and the spots on my body are erased. O Keeper of the Portal, make the path for me, for I am one of you. Let me come forth by day and walk on my legs. Let me have the feet of the Glorified. I know the mysterious paths and gates of Aarru from where I come. Here I am, to overthrow my adversaries on earth, though my body is buried. If this chapter is known, he will re-enter after coming forth by day.

Chapter LXXXVII: Transforming into Se-ta

I am Se-ta, full of years. I lay down in death and am born daily. I am Se-ta at the earth's edges. I lay down in death, restore myself, and renew myself daily.

Chapter LXXXVIII: Transforming into the Crocodile God (Sebak)

I am the Crocodile God in all his terrors. I am the Crocodile God in human form. I am he who takes with violence. I am the almighty Fish in Kamurit. I am the Lord to whom one bows in Sechem.### Chapter LXXXIX: Reuniting the Soul with the Body

Oh, you who bring and you who run, dwelling in your keep, great God, grant that my soul may return to me from wherever it resides. If there is a delay in reuniting my soul with me, you will find the Eye of Horus standing firm against you, like the vigilant Watchers in Annu, the land of countless reunions. Let my soul and the spirit (Chu) with it be found, no matter where they are. Track my soul across heaven and earth. If there is a delay in showing me my soul and my shade, you will face the Eye of Horus. Oh Gods who guide the Bark of the Eternal One, who lift the sky and enable souls to enter mummified forms, hold firm with your ropes and stop the adversaries so the Bark may rejoice and the God proceed in peace. Grant that my soul may come forth with you from the Eastern horizon of Heaven forever.

### Chapter XC: Restoring Memory

Oh, you who chop off heads and cut throats but restore memory in the mouths of the dead through Words of Power, you do not see me with your eyes or perceive me with your feet. You turn back your face and do not see the executioners of Shu coming to chop off your head and cut your throat. Let my mouth not be closed through the Words of Power I possess, just as you have done for the dead through their Words of Power. Away with the two sentences uttered by Isis when she brought remembrance to the mouth of Osiris and the heart of Sutu, his enemy.

### Chapter XCI: Securing the Soul from Imprisonment

Oh, exalted and worshipped one, almighty, who grants terrors to the Gods and displays grandeur on your throne, make a way for my soul, my spirit (Chu), and my shade. Let me be fully equipped. I am a powerful soul; make a way for me to where Ra and Hathor are. If this chapter is known, one takes the form of a fully equipped spirit in the Netherworld and does not suffer imprisonment at any door in the Afterlife, either coming in or going out.

### Chapter XCII: Opening the Tomb

Oh, you who open and close, who are at rest, open and close for my soul at the bidding of the Eye of Horus, who delivers me and establishes glory upon the brow of Ra. The God of stretched-out steps and rapid paces makes a wide path and vigorous limbs for me. I am Horus, the avenger of his father, who lifts up his father and mother with his staff. Let the path be opened to him who has mastery of his feet, so he may look upon the great God within the Bark of Ra on the day of the Soul's Reckoning. My soul will be at the front during the Reckoning of the Years.

### Chapter XCIII: Avoiding Being Taken to the East

Oh, Phallus of Ra, who flees from the storm, disablement arises from Baba, who uses might beyond the mighty and power beyond the powerful against me. If I am taken to the East, if all evil and injurious things of a feast day of fiends are done to me through the waving of the Two Horns, then the Phallus of Ra and the Head of Osiris will be devoured. If I am led to the fields where the Gods destroy those who answer them, the horns of Chepera will be twisted back, blindness will arise in the eyes of Tmu, and destruction will come through my seizure and being taken to the East.### Chapter XCV: Opening the Place Where Thoth Rests

I am the Fearsome One in the Storm, protecting the Great One from attacks. I strike like the Flint-God and sprinkle like the Sprinkling-God. I guard the Great One from harm and empower the sword in Thoth's hand during the storm.

### Chapter XCVI: Opening the Place Where Thoth Rests

I dwell within my own Eye. I come to deliver Maat to Ra and offer libations to Sutu for Akar and the faithful of Seb.

### Chapter XCVII: At the Bark

Staff of Anubis, may I appease the four Glorified Ones who follow the Master of all things. I am the Master of the fields at their command and the Father of the flood when the canal keeper is thirsty. Look upon me, great and mighty Gods, foremost among the Spirits of Annu. Let me be exalted in your presence. I come to purify my Soul to the highest degree. Do not let any impediment from your mouth ruin me. Let me be purified in the lake of propitiation and balance. Let me plunge into the divine pool beneath the two divine sycamores of Heaven and Earth. Let my Fold be fitted for me as one victorious against all adversaries who deny me justice. I am the Only One, just and true upon the Earth. It is I who say it.

### Chapter XCVIII: Sailing a Ship in the Netherworld

Oh Leg in the Northern Sky, in that conspicuous but inaccessible Stream, I rise and come to light as a God. I am conspicuous but inaccessible. I rise and live, bringing myself to light as a God. I cackle like the Smen-goose but stoop like the Hawk at the nets of the Great Fowler. I sail across the Sky, and Shu stands erect. The Achmiu Stars instantly raise the ladder that lifts the Setting Stars from destruction. I repel mischief as I voyage over the Leg of Ptah. I come from the Lake of Flame, the Lake of Fire, and the Field of Flame. I live and stand erect in the Bark piloted by the God at the head of Aarru. The Achmiu Stars open to me, and my fellow citizens present me with sacred cakes and flesh.

### Chapter XCIX: Sailing a Ship in the Netherworld

Oh you who sail the ship of Nu over the void, let me sail the ship and fasten my tackle in peace. Come, come, Fleet One! Let me see my father Osiris. Oh veiled one, let me enjoy happiness. Oh clouded but manful one, who sails over the chine of Apepi, firm-headed and steadfast when emerging from fiery blows, let me sail the ship and fasten my tackle. This place is empty, where the starry ones fall headlong and cannot rise. The path is narrow like the tongue of Ra. The Patrol who pilots the Double Earth, Seb abides by their rudders. The divine Form reveals the Solar Orb, and He presides over the Red ones. Let me be brought in as a distressed mariner, and let my Soul, my brother, go to that place you know. "Tell me my name," I say. The Mooring post: "Lord of the Double-Earth in the Shrine" is your name. The Blade of the Rudder: "Leg of Apis" is your name. The Hawser: "The Side-Lock which Anubis fastens on to the swathing work" is your name. The Stern or Stem Posts: "The two columns of the Netherworld" is your name. The Hold: "Akar" is your name. The Mast: "Bearer of the Great One while she passes" is your name. The Keel: "Backbone of Apuat" is your name. The Mast-head: "Throat of Emsta" is your name. The Sail: "Nut" is your name. The Leathers: "Made of the hide of Mnevis, which Sutu scorched" is your name. The Oars: "Fingers of the elder" is your name. The Bracement: "Hand of Isis, stanching the blood" is your name.### Chapter XCIX: Sailing a Ship in the Netherworld

Oh, you who sail the ship of Nu over the void, let me sail the ship and secure my gear in peace. Come, come, Swift One! Let me see my father Osiris. Oh veiled one, let me enjoy happiness.
