The lion-headed God, sluggishness, and other divine attributes are also discussed.

15. Thou of the Bright Teeth: This phrase refers to a deity known for their bright teeth, symbolizing clarity or brilliance. The Demotic equivalent is "who openeth his teeth," highlighting their brightness.

16. Aati: This name, often misinterpreted by copyists, is one of Ra's names in the Solar Litany, meaning "Cutter" or "that which cleaves its way." It has been misread by scholars as Teti or Chonti.

17. Tufu: This name has many variants, showing that scribes did not understand its meaning. It appears with different determinatives, including a snake or a bird of evil. The God Tutu, associated with Neith, is symbolized by a serpent or slug.

18. I trouble myself only with my own affairs: This phrase refers to the virtue of minding one's own business, as discussed by Cicero and Plato. It opposes the behavior of busybodies who meddle in others' affairs.

19. A, or Amu: This name refers to a town in northern Egypt, possibly identified with Apis. In rituals, Horus is depicted raising Osiris's body from the water as a crocodile, and Osiris is called "The Crocodile, Lord of Amu."

20. Chemiu: This name means "one who overthrows" and is associated with a deity appearing at the entrance to the Nile. It may refer to violations of ritual precepts.

21. Who raises thy voice words of Righteousness: This attribute is assigned to Isis, known for her clear and powerful speech. She is described as "Mighty in Words of Power" and "Most potent and unfailing of speech."

22. Hot of foot: This phrase refers to a passion that is laudable in Gods but blameworthy in humans. The divine wrath is just, while human anger is imperfect.

23. Kenemta: This God, identified with a cynocephalus, is associated with the constellation occupying the month of Thoth. The name means "in Ape form."

This modernized version aims to make the ancient text more accessible and understandable to contemporary readers.In the Pyramid Texts (Pepi I, 408, and Merira 579), the term is used to mean 'vested,' 'clad,' or simply 'covered.' Brugsch identified the locality Kenemit with the Great Oasis at Khargeh. Its uncertain if the Oasis bore this name when this chapter was composed. The determinative suggests that "Dark" might be a sufficient translation. From the etymology, it could be related to the Greek term for division.

23. Of inconstant mind: Another interpretation of the precept is, "I do not rob the dead of their wrappings," but the text is so corrupt that none of the readings are reliable. The God is called "busy-minded," "planning," "devising," or "wise." The term "Horned one" is equivalent to the Hebrew term for Osiris, especially in the character he was worshipped under at Sutenhunen.

24. Noisy in speech: This is a name of Horus, as noted in Chapter 103.

25. There is no agreed-upon locality in the older papyri, and many omit mentioning a locality. Later texts, like the Turin text, read "Annu."

26. No unjust preferences: This virtue is frequently praised on funerary monuments, where great personages declare they made no distinction between great and small, rich or poor, wise or simple.

27. Of raised head: This is a name of the Nile God, one of Osiris's manifestations.

28. Who lifts an arm: This phrase means to support or hold up, not to bring. The God Shu, who supports the sky, is an example.

29. This introduction to Part III of this chapter occurs only in the Papyrus of Nebkat. Another manuscript has the words "Said upon approaching triumphantly to the Hall of Righteousness." Generally, texts begin with "Hail ye Gods, I know you and I know your names."

30. Reverse of mine: This implies an unfortunate turn of events. An absurd reading suggests the defendant controls the fates of his divine judges.

31. The King who resides within His own Day: This passage is doubtful and does not occur in the oldest text of the chapter. Some papyri have a similar phrase, but the exact meaning is unclear.

32. Cares: The older texts differ greatly, but the most frequent reading is "cares."

33. The Ass and the Cat in the house of Hept-ro: These characters are known from other parts of the Book of the Dead. The Cat is Ra, and the Ass appears as the victim of the devouring Serpent. The Sun-God overcome by darkness is Osiris.

34. Covereth: The right Egyptian word is uncertain, but the meaning is clear. Many pictures show a divinity hidden within or behind a tree.

35. That the Balance may be set upon its stand within the bower of amaranth: This passage mentions divine powers lifting the Balance before them. Amaranth is one of the readings of this text.

36. Disasters: The word means misfortune.

37. Grasshoppers: The word is familiar in Egyptian and serves as a term for comparison, "as plentiful as grasshoppers."

38. The text here is uncertain. Different papyri have varying readings for the hours of the Night and Day.

39. The hearts of the Gods are appeased: This phrase explains the appeasement of the Gods.

40. Let him come: The reading is certain, but the preceding word is unclear. Scribes have written various interpretations.

41. He who groweth under the Grass: This phrase is used in the text.

42. A thigh: This term is used in the text.

43. See the greetings: This phrase is used in the text.

44. The Leaf: This term is used in the text.

45. Pointer (or Plummet) of Truth: This term is used in the text.

46. The Scale Pan: This term is used in the text.

47. The Dragon Brood: This term is used in the text.

48. The Truncheon of Hathor: This word is shown by its determinative to be of wood and is used for striking, blinding, or slaying. Some texts name Hathor, others Nephthys.

49. He who knoweth the heart and exploreth the person: This phrase is used in the text.This passage is similar to the biblical phrase "searching the heart and trying the reins" from Jeremiah 17:10. However, the Coptic Bible closely follows the Septuagint's sense, even using specific Greek words. Thoth is depicted as divine Providence, caring for the universe, a view also found in Edfu texts.

Chapter CXXVI:
"Oh, you four Harbingers who sit at the prow of Ra's Bark, conveying the fixed laws of the Inviolate One, judges of my distress and good fortune, who appease the Gods with flames from your mouths, presenting oblations and sacrificial meals to the Glorified, living through Maat and sated with Maat, who have nothing wrong in you and detest disorder, please end my ills and remove disorder from me as I am smitten to the earth. Grant me entry into Ammehit and Restau, and passage through the mysterious portals of Amenta. May I receive the Shensu and Persen cakes."

Notes:
1. Harbingers or Saluters: These are the Apes who greet the Daybreak, originally four in number, corresponding to the four portals of the Mount of Glory. The number eight (Chemunnu) is easier to explain than six, as stated in the tomb of Rameses VI.
2. Fixed ordinances: This term has various meanings.
3. Distress: This term implies need or constraint rather than captivity. Amenemhat at Benihassan claimed no one was seen in distress or starving under his rule. Horus at Edfu is said to protect the needy against the powerful.
4. Disordered: This term means the absence of strict order, not necessarily wickedness or sin, but physical evil, mischief, pain, or sorrow. Osiris is invoked at Apu as the fiery Bull, rising into full strength and seeing the Golden Horus on the throne of the universe. Joy follows pain, not sin.
5. Through my being smitten to the earth: This phrase indicates a cause or circumstance connected to a preceding statement. It is used to explain the reason behind an action or condition.
6. The older texts end here. The later recensions include the reply of the four Harbingers to the prayer.
7. Mount of Glory: This term is more accurate than the misleading term "horizon."

Chapter CXXVII:
The Book for invoking...Chapter CXXVII:
The Book for invoking the Gods of the Boundaries, which the person recites when approaching them, to enter and see the Strong One in the Great Abode of the Tuat. 

"Hail, Gods of the Boundaries in Amenta. Hail, Doorkeepers of the Tuat, who guard the Strong One and report to Osiris. You protect those who worship you and destroy Ra's enemies. You bring light and dispel darkness. You see and praise your Great One, living as he lives, and invoke him in his Solar disk. Guide me and open the gates of Heaven, Earth, and the Tuat for me. I am the Soul of Osiris and rest in him. Let me pass through the Gateways, and let them cheer when they see me. Let me enter and exit as I please, without any defect or evil attached to me."

Notes:
1. The text followed here is from the Royal Tombs of Rameses IV and VI, called Chapter 127a by M. Naville. The lost Busca papyrus, traced by Lepsius, offers a different text (127b), and the Turin Todtenbuch text has many interpolations. M. Naville noted the close relationship between this chapter and the second part of the "Solar Litany."
2. "Bounds" is not a direct translation of the Egyptian term, which needs explanation from the "Solar Litany." The Sun-God Ra is invoked as a Power overflowing. Each divine form has its own dwelling place, not confined to it. The seventy-five Forms are names of the Solar God or phenomena, each addressed as 'Ra, supreme of power,' with an attribute. In Greek mythology, Apollo had many names expressing his attributes, similar to Egyptian mythology's concept of a God's form. M. de Rouge translated the word as "zone," while M. Naville preferred "sphere." The Egyptian term was a hollow cylinder, like a round tower or deep well, rather than a sphere. "Bounds" is a more expressive translation. The name was given to the mythical Source of the Nile, near Elephantine. The inscription of Seti I at Redesieh compares the abundance of water at the King's cistern to the "cavern of the Double Well of Elephantine." The later orthography writes it differently. The Coptic word for cataracts might be connected to the old Egyptian name, but its history is unclear.
3. The Strong One is Osiris. See Chapter 126, Note 4.

Chapter CXXVIII:
Invocation of Osiris:
"Hail to you, Osiris Unneferu, son of Nut and eldest son of Seb: the Great One from Nut; the king in Taa-urit; the Prince in Amenta; the Lord of Abydos; the Lord of Forces; the most Mighty; the Lord of the Atef crown in Suten-hunen, the Lord of Power in Taa-urit; the Lord of the Mansion: most Powerful in Tattu; Lord of Administration, and of many festivals in Tattu. Horus exalts his father Osiris everywhere, associating Isis the Great with her sister Nephthys. Thoth speaks to Horus with potent utterances, strengthening Horus's heart beyond all Gods. Rise up Horus, son of Isis, and restore your father Osiris! Ha, Osiris! I am here; I am Horus and I restore you to life today, with funereal offerings and all good things for Osiris. Rise up, Osiris: I have defeated your enemies and delivered you from them. I am Horus on this fair day, at the beautiful coming forth of your Powers: who lifts you up with himself on this fair day as your associate God. Ha, Osiris! you have come with your Ka, which unites with you in your name of Ka-hotep. He glorifies you in your name of the Glorified: he invokes you in your name of Hekau: he opens paths for you in your name of Ap-uat. Ha, Osiris! I am here to set your adversaries beneath you everywhere, so you may be triumphant before all the Gods around you. Ha, Osiris! you have received your sceptre, your pedestal, and the flight of stairs beneath you. Regulate the festivals of the Gods, and the oblations to those in their mansions. Grant your greatness to the Gods you made, great God, and appear with them as their Ensign. Take precedence over all the Gods and listen to the Voice of Maat today."

Said over the oblations made to the Strong One on the Festival of Uaka.

Notes:
1. The ancient papyri do not contain this chapter. The translation follows the Turin Todtenbuch text, occasionally corrected by other later period papyri. The chapter is an invocation to Osiris under certain names, similar to many other hymns to the God from the XIIth dynasty to later times. The latter part consists of evocations by Horus to his father, modeled after formulas in the Pyramid Texts, admired and imitated in the Saitic and later periods.
2. Osiris is also called "King in Tau-urit" at Philae. In the second line of this chapter, he is called "in Tau-urit," which, if not identical with Abydos, must have been part of or near that town.
3. "Administration" literally means "things." See note 3 on Chapter 18.
4. "Utterances" are potent words. See note 2 on Chapter 1, and compare Merenra, 103, and Pepi II, 13.
5. "Coming forth" refers to daybreak. The first hour after sunrise was called "the beautiful Coming forth of your Powers," a technical term for daybreak. Remember such proper names as "Ra in Chapter 17," and others.
6. "Thine associate God" or one of those around you. See Note 2 on Chapter 18. M. Chabas noted that Osiris is included among his 'Djadjou,' explained by parallel expressions in Greek, meaning the person with their followers.
7. This passage is an alteration of one of the Pyramid Texts (Teta, 284; Pepi I, 54): "Horus..."Osiris, the Unneferu, son of Nut and eldest son of Seb, the Great One from Nut, the king in Taa-urit, the Prince in Amenta, the Lord of Abydos, the Lord of Forces, the most Mighty, the Lord of the Atef crown in Suten-hunen, the Lord of Power in Taa-urit, the Lord of the Mansion, most Powerful in Tattu, Lord of Administration, and of many festivals in Tattu. Horus exalts his father Osiris everywhere, associating Isis the Great with her sister Nephthys. Thoth speaks to Horus with potent utterances, strengthening Horus's heart beyond all Gods. Rise up Horus, son of Isis, and restore your father Osiris! Ha, Osiris! I am here; I am Horus and I restore you to life today, with funereal offerings and all good things for Osiris. Rise up, Osiris: I have defeated your enemies and delivered you from them. I am Horus on this fair day, at the beautiful coming forth of your Powers: who lifts you up with himself on this fair day as your associate God. Ha, Osiris! you have come with your Ka, which unites with you in your name of Ka-hotep. He glorifies you in your name of the Glorified: he invokes you in your name of Hekau: he opens paths for you in your name of Ap-uat. Ha, Osiris! I am here to set your adversaries beneath you everywhere, so you may be triumphant before all the Gods around you. Ha, Osiris! you have received your sceptre, your pedestal, and the flight of stairs beneath you. Regulate the festivals of the Gods, and the oblations to those in their mansions. Grant your greatness to the Gods you made, great God, and appear with them as their Ensign. Take precedence over all the Gods and listen to the Voice of Maat today.

Said over the oblations made to the Strong One on the Festival of Uaka.

Notes:
1. The ancient papyri do not contain this chapter. The translation follows the Turin Todtenbuch text, occasionally corrected by other later period papyri. The chapter is an invocation to Osiris under certain names, similar to many other hymns to the God from the XIIth dynasty to later times. The latter part consists of evocations by Horus to his father, modeled after formulas in the Pyramid Texts, admired and imitated in the Saitic and later periods.
2. Osiris is also called "King in Tau-urit" at Philae. In the second line of this chapter, he is called "in Tau-urit," which, if not identical with Abydos, must have been part of or near that town.

7. This passage is an alteration of one of the Pyramid Texts (Teta, 284; Pepi I, 54): "Horus..."

Chapter CXXIX is a repetition of Chapter C.

Chapter CXXX:
A Book whereby the Soul is made to live forever, on the day of entering into the Bark of Ra, and to pass the Shemzi of the Tuat. Made on the Birthday of Osiris,

(1) Opened be the gates of Heaven; opened be the gates of Earth; opened be the gates of the East; opened be the gates of the West; opened be the gates of the Southern and of the Northern sanctuaries. Opened be the gates and thrown wide the portals as Ra riseth up from the Mount of Glory; opened to him be the doors of the Sektit boat, thrown open to him be the portals of the Maatit, as he scenteth Shu and setteth in motion Tefnut, and those follow who are in the train of the Osiris N, who followeth Ra and taketh possession of his arms of steel.

(2) I am coffined in an ark like Horus, to whom his cradle is brought: and secret is the place, hard by his own shrine, which the God openeth to whom he willeth. And so it cometh that I lift up Right to the Lord of Right, and that I make fast the cord which windeth about the shrine. The Osiris N avoideth the raging storm: the Osiris N is not to be kept away from Ra, not to be repulsed is he. Let not the Osiris N advance into the Valley of Darkness: let not the Osiris N enter into the dungeon of the captives: let him not leap into the grip of Fate, let him not fall among those who imprison souls or come forth among those who would drag him behind the slaughtering block of the Armed God.

(3) Salutations to you, ye sejant Gods. The divine Sword is concealed in the hands of Seb, at daybreak, for he delighteth in drawing to himself both old and young at his own season. And now behold Thoth in the secret of his mysteries. He maketh purifications and endless reckonings; piercing the steel firmament and dissipating the storms around him. And so it cometh that the Osiris N hath reached every station of his. He hath fashioned his staff, and received the oblations of Ra, the swift of speed and beautiful in his rising and almighty through what he hath done. He putteth an end to his pain and suffering, and the Osiris N putteth an end to his own pain; yea, he gladdeneth the countenance of Thoth by the worship of Ra and Osiris. The Osiris N entereth the Mount of Glory of Ra, who hath made his Bark and saileth prosperously, lightening up the face of Thoth, that he may listen to Ra and beat down the obstacles in his way, and put an end to his adversaries. Let not the Osiris N be shipwrecked on the great voyage by him whose face is in his own lap: for the name of Ra is upon the Osiris, and his token of honour is on his mouth, which speaketh to him who listeneth to the words of the Osiris N.

Glory to thee, O Ra, Lord of the Mount of Glory. Hail to thee, who purifiest the generations yet unborn and to whom this great quarter of heaven offereth homage. The steering keepeth clear from misadventure. Lo, here is Osiris who proclaimeth Right, because of the marvel in the West, for he hath put an end to the rage of Apepi, for he is himself the God in Lion form among the associate Gods and protecteth Ra against Apepi daily, that he may not approach him, and he keepeth watch upon him. Osiris seizeth the scrolls and receiveth the offerings. And Thoth supplieth the Osiris N with that which he shall perform for him. It is granted that the Osiris shall carry Maat at the head of the great Bark, and hold up Maat among the associate Gods, and that Osiris gain endless triumphs. The Sheniu marshal the Osiris N, and they procure for the Osiris a voyage amid acclamations. The Satellites of Ra make their round, in the train of the exaltation of Maat, who followeth her Lord. And glory is given to the Inviolate one. The Osiris receiveth the Amsu-staff wherewith he goeth round Heaven. The unborn generations of men give him glory, as to one who standeth without ever resting. Ra exalteth him by this, that he alloweth the Osiris to disperse the cloud and behold his glories. He maketh firm his rudders that the Bark may go round in Heaven and that he may make his appearance in Antu. Thoth is in the centre of his eye, sejant in the great Bark of Chepera. The Osiris becometh one whose words come to pass. He it is who passeth over Heaven unto the West, and the Chabasu Gods of Light rise up to him with acclamation. They receive the cable of Ra from his rowers, and Ra goeth on his round and seeth the Osiris who issueth his decrees; the Osiris N, the Victorious; in peace! in peace! Not to be repelled is he; not to be caught by the fire of thy fate. Let not the tempest of thy mouth come forth against him. Let not the Osiris N advance upon the paths of misfortune: let him avoid disasters, let them not attain him. The Osiris N enters into the Bark of Ra, he succeedeth to thy throne; he receiveth thine insignia. The Osiris N inaugurateth the paths of Ra and prayeth that he may drive off the Lock which cometh out of the flame against thy Bark out of the great Stream. But the Osiris N knoweth it, and it attaineth not thy Bark. For the Osiris N is within it; the Osiris N who maketh the divine offerings.

Said over a Bark of Ra, colored in pure green, and thou shalt place a picture of the deceased at the prow thereof. And make a Sektit boat on the right side of it and an Auit boat.on the left side of it.

Notes:
1. This title is given to the chapter in later versions and is similar to the one in the Berlin papyrus of Nechtu-amen (from the 19th dynasty). Another older papyrus has a different title, "Chapter whereby the Chu is fortified." Instead of the Sheniu of the Tieat, the papyrus of Nechtuamen has the Sheniu of Fire. The Sheniu in this chapter are living beings who attend to Osiris and greet him with acclamations. The term is often translated as 'princes' or 'officers,' but it means those in the circle of a king or God, hence 'ministrants' or 'courtiers,' as in the rubric of Chapter CXXV. The words made on the Birth-day of Osiris are only found in later texts, but the old papyrus has another title and includes the words for the Birth-day of Osiris, which was the first of the five supplementary days added to the year of 360 days. On this day, the chapter was to be recited, and the usual offerings made.

2. Arms of steel.

3. Cradle or Nest, often represented in pictures of later periods.

4. The Armed God, depicted as a hawk armed with bow and arrows, sometimes in the form of Bes, destroyer of the Menti.

5. Sejant Gods, a term used to describe Gods sitting on the ground with their knees raised against their chests, a common posture in Egyptian pictures.

6. This divine Sword, representing unseen fate that brings down the old and young alike to the grave, always ready to receive them. Seb is often referenced in relation to the dead in the Tuat.

7. Whose face is in his own lap.

8. The Amsu staff, an emblem of both Osiris and Horus, often represented with bows, arrows, and other weapons in the oldest coffins.

9. Who issues his decrees.

10. Green, likely meaning pale green or yellowish-green.

11. The rubric ends here, with additional instructions to offer bread, beer, and all good things on the Birth-day of Osiris. If these rites are performed, the soul will rise and live forever, never dying a second time in the divine Netherworld. Later texts add that the text was discovered in the great hall of the palace during the time of King Septa and found in a pit or chamber in the rock. It was made by Horus for his father Osiris Unneferu. Septa is the fifth royal name on the great tablet of Abydos.

Chapter CXXXI: Chapter whereby one proceeds into Heaven by the side of Ra.

1. Oh Ra, who shines this night: if any among your followers presents himself alive as a follower of Thoth, who brings forth Horus this night, the heart of Osiris is glad because he leads them. His adversaries are stopped by the warriors of Osiris N, who follows Ra and has taken his arms of steel. He comes to you, his father Ra, follows Shu, and calls for the Crown. He puts on Hu and is adorned with the Lock on Ra's path, his glory. He arrives at the Aged one, at the Mount of Glory, and the crown awaits him. Osiris N raises it up. Your Soul is with you, strong through the terror and might that belong to you, Oh Osiris N, who utters the decrees spoken by Ra in Heaven. Hail to you, great God in the East of Heaven, who enters the Bark of Ra as the Divine Hawk and executes the decrees. Osiris N enters your Bark and sails peacefully to the Fair West. Tniu says to him: Are you coming in? Mehenit is millions upon millions in length from Amur to Ta-ur, an endless river where the Gods move, whose path is in the fire, and they travel in the fire who come behind him.

Notes:
1. None of the oldest papyri contain this chapter, but this does not argue against its antiquity. The latter part of the text is very corrupt, and we have no means of correcting it.

2. Oh Ra. The name of the God is sometimes omitted in manuscripts, but the context requires its presence. The Sun-God shines in the night through Thoth, the Moon.

3. Warriors.

4. He puts on Hu. This is obscure but aligns with the doctrine of the Pyramid texts. The deceased is fed from night till daybreak and then seizes upon the God Hu. After Sau is fastened to his feet, he enters the bark and seizes the Mount of Glory.

5. Mehenit, a mythological serpent symbolizing the Sun's nightly course from West to East. It is represented as extending over the shrine in which the Sun-God is borne in his Bark. The serpent's many folds symbolize the river or canal's turnings and windings, described as infinite in length.

6. There is a corrupt passage here, which cannot be corrected by manuscript authority. M. Pierret translates it as: "The God who shares the words makes his path of millions of years, a lord without equal, whose path is in the fire."

Chapter CXXXII: Chapter whereby a person is enabled to go round, to visit his dwelling in the Netherworld.

I am the Lion-God who issues from the Bow, and therefore have I shot forth. I am the Eye of Horus, and the Eye of Horus is opened when I reach the strand, coming with a happy outcome. I advance, and there is no defect found in me, and the Balance is relieved of my case.

Notes:
1. The Bow, often written with the determinative of stretching, is the moon's crescent, always turned towards the sun. This observation explains why the sun is spoken of as shining in or from the moon.

2. I follow the Turin text in omitting a word about which earlier texts disagree.

3. See the end of Chapter 1 and note. These words are omitted in the Turin text.

Chapter CXXXIII: Book whereby the Deceased acquires Might in the Netherworld in the presence of the great Cycle of the Gods.

Said on the first day of the Month. Ra makes his appearance at the Mount of Glory, with the Cycle of Gods around him: the Strong one issues from his hidden abode.Chapter CXXXI: How to Ascend to Heaven with Ra

1. Oh Ra, who shines tonight: If any of your followers presents themselves alive as a follower of Thoth, who brings forth Horus tonight, Osiris's heart is glad because he leads them. His enemies are stopped by Osiris N's warriors, who follow Ra and have taken his steel arms. He comes to you, his father Ra, follows Shu, and calls for the Crown. He puts on Hu and is adorned with the Lock on Ra's path, his glory. He arrives at the Aged one, at the Mount of Glory, and the crown awaits him. Osiris N raises it up. Your Soul is with you, strong through the terror and might that belong to you, Oh Osiris N, who utters the decrees spoken by Ra in Heaven. Hail to you, great God in the East of Heaven, who enters the Bark of Ra as the Divine Hawk and executes the decrees. Osiris N enters your Bark and sails peacefully to the Fair West. Tniu says to him: Are you coming in? Mehenit is millions upon millions in length from Amur to Ta-ur, an endless river where the Gods move, whose path is in the fire, and they travel in the fire who come behind him.

Notes:
1. None of the oldest papyri contain this chapter, but this does not argue against its antiquity. The latter part of the text is very corrupt, and we have no means of correcting it.

2. Oh Ra. The name of the God is sometimes omitted in manuscripts, but the context requires its presence. The Sun-God shines in the night through Thoth, the Moon.

3. Warriors.

4. He puts on Hu. This is obscure but aligns with the doctrine of the Pyramid texts. The deceased is fed from night till daybreak and then seizes upon the God Hu. After Sau is fastened to his feet, he enters the bark and seizes the Mount of Glory.

5. Mehenit, a mythological serpent symbolizing the Sun's nightly course from West to East. It is represented as extending over the shrine in which the Sun-God is borne in his Bark. The serpent's many folds symbolize the river or canal's turnings and windings, described as infinite in length.

6. There is a corrupt passage here, which cannot be corrected by manuscript authority. M. Pierret translates it as: "The God who shares the words makes his path of millions of years, a lord without equal, whose path is in the fire."

Chapter CXXXII: How to Visit Your Dwelling in the Netherworld

I am the Lion-God who issues from the Bow, and therefore have I shot forth. I am the Eye of Horus, and the Eye of Horus is opened when I reach the strand, coming with a happy outcome. I advance, and there is no defect found in me, and the Balance is relieved of my case.

Notes:
1. The Bow, often written with the determinative of stretching, is the moon's crescent, always turned towards the sun. This observation explains why the sun is spoken of as shining in or from the moon.

2. I follow the Turin text in omitting a word about which earlier texts disagree.

3. See the end of Chapter 1 and note. These words are omitted in the Turin text.

Chapter CXXXIII: How the Deceased Gains Power in the Netherworld

Said on the first day of the Month. Ra makes his appearance at the Mount of Glory, with the Cycle of Gods around him: the Strong one issues from his hidden abode.

Twinklers fall away from the Mount of Glory at the East of Heaven, at the voice of Nut as she builds up the paths of Ra, before the Ancient one who goes round. Be lifted up, O Ra who is in your shrine; breathe the breezes, inhale the north wind on the day when you discern the Land of Maat. You divide those that follow; the Bark advances and the Ancient ones step onwards at your voice. Reckon your bones, and set your limbs, and turn your face towards the beautiful Amenta. For you are the golden Form, with a couch of the heavenly orbs, with the Twinklers among whom you go round, and are renewed daily. Acclamation comes from the Mount of Glory, and greeting from the lines of measurement. The Gods who are in heaven see Osiris N, they present to him their adorations as to Ra. He is the Great one, who seeks the Crown and reckons up what is needed. He is the One, who comes forth this day from the primeval womb of those who were before Ra, and his coming forth takes place upon earth and in the Netherworld. His coming forth is like Ra daily. Without haste, but unresting, is Osiris N on this Land of Eternity. Twice blessed is he that sees with his eyes and hears with his ears. Right, right is Osiris N: and his future, his future, is in Annu. His oars are lifted as in the service of Nu. Osiris N has not told what he has seen; he has not repeated what he has heard in the house of the God who hides his face. There are hailing and cries of welcome to Osiris N, the divine body of Ra, on traversing the Nu, and while the ka of the God is being propitiated, according to his pleasure. Osiris N is the Hawk, rich in variety of Forms. The Deceased acquires might with Ra, and is enabled to possess power among the Gods, for the Gods are made to regard him as one of themselves, and when the Dead ones see him they fall upon their faces. He is seen in the Netherworld even as the beams of Ra. Said over a Boat of four cubits in length, painted green. And let a starry sky be made, clean and purified with natron and incense. And see you make an image of Ra upon a tablet of light green color at the prow of the Boat. And see you make an image of the Deceased whom you love, that he may be made strong in this boat, and that his voyage be made in the Bark of Ra, and that Ra himself may look upon him. Do not do this for anyone except for yourself, your father, and your son. And let them be exceedingly cautious for themselves. The Deceased acquires might with Ra, and is made to possess power among the Gods, who regard him as one of themselves, and when men or the Dead see him they fall upon their faces. He is seen in the Netherworld as the image of Ra.

Notes:
1. The earliest known text of this chapter is from the Tomb of Amenemhait at Thebes, from the time of Thothmes III. It is almost as inaccurate as that of Nebseni or the Brockelhurst Ax. Nor is the text of Ani of any use towards clearing up any of the difficulties.

2. Acquireth Might. The term does not signify wise, nor has it anything to do with instruction or perfection, as supposed by other translators. As an adjective, it is used to qualify not only animate but inanimate things, such as an egg, beer, and incense. The well-known expressions exactly correspond to the Hebrew terms. The notion implied, as in the Hebrew, is that of strength. In the Prisse Papyrus, it is not a wise man, but a powerful one, a man of rank or influence. This is the meaning of the word in such passages. These expressions are the exact equivalents of the Greek term. The might acquired by the deceased is stated in the final rubric and in all the titles of the chapter in the later recensions to be with reference to Ra.

3. Said on the first day of the Month. These words first appear on the Papyrus of Ani.

4. The Twinklers. The oldest texts in this place have though the equivalent and corresponding word a little further on is which is the usual reading here in the later recensions. The same meaning may be made out of both groups. The stars are manifestly alluded to, as being made to disappear when the Sun makes his appearance. The glance of the eye is characterized by their tremulous motion. The stars are here considered as so many eyes, characterized by their tremulous motion.

5. The true text is here quite lost. Some sense might be restored if we might read instead of the latter word is absolute nonsense in this place, whatever determinative it may have, but the former is the well-known name of a tree held sacred at various places in Egypt. The whole passage then might mean "Enjoy the north wind, and may the Kabasu trees of your abode refresh you."

6. The golden Form. The whole of this passage will become clear after reading the final rubric and examining the Vignettes of the chapter.

7. Line of measurement. The explanation of this will be found in the pictures and text of the Book of Hades. In Bonomi's Sarcophagus, twelve personages are represented in the act of acclamation, and twelve others carry the line intended for the line is stated in the text. "The bearers of the line are those who settle the fields of the Chu. They are called upon to take their line and to fix the arable land of each allotment. Ra expresses his satisfaction at the measurement and tells the Gods and the Chu that their domains are theirs, and that he provides their food.

8. The rubric is taken from Ax.

Chapter CXXXIV: How the Deceased Gains Might

Hail to you who are in the midst of your Ark, Oh rising Sun who rises, and declining one who declines: at whose will millions spring forth, as he turns his face to the unborn generations of men: Chepera in the middle of his Bark, who overthrows Apepi. Here are the children of Seb who overthrow the adversaries of Osiris and destroy them from the Bark of Ra. Horus cuts off their heads in heaven when in the forms of winged fowl, their hinder parts on earth when in the forms of quadrupeds or in the water as fishes. All fiends, male or female, Osiris N destroys them, whether descending from heaven or coming forth upon the earth, or issuing out of the water or traveling along with the Stars. Thoth slaughters them, the Son of the Rock, proceeding from the place of the Two Rocks. Osiris N is dumb and deaf for the Strong one is Ra, the puissant of stroke, the Almighty one, who washes in their blood and wallows in their gore. Osiris N destroys them from the Bark of his father Ra. Osiris N is Horus: his mother Isis brings him forth, and Nephthys nurses him, as they did to Horus, who repels the dark ones of Sutu: who, when they see the Crown fixed upon his brow, fall upon their faces. Osiris Unneferu is triumphant over his adversaries in heaven and on earth, and in the cycle of each God and Goddess. Said over a Hawk in a Boat, with the White Crown upon its head, and the figure of Tnni, Shu, Tefnut, Seb, Nut, Osiris, Isis, Sutu, Nephthys, painted yellowish green on a fresh papyrus placed in this Boat, together with the figure of the Deceased, anointed with the Heknu oil. Let there be offered to them incense burning and roast fowl. It is the adoration of Ra, and his voyage, for it is granted to him to make his appearance each day with Ra, wherever he journeys; and it is the Slaughter of the adversaries of Ra; positively and undeviatingly for times infinite.

Notes:
1. Declining. This word frequently occurs in contrast with the shining of the sun on his rising, and the former to signify the shining of the sun in his afternoon course.

2. The son of the Rock, proceeding from the place of the Two Rocks. The only explanation I can think of is derived from the identification of Thoth with the Nile. From this point of view, the God is both the son of the Rock and issues from the place of the Double Rock, or of the two Rocks, called in the time of Herodotus Krophi and Mophi.

3. Dumb and deaf. It is strange that this meaning of the passage has so long been misunderstood. The sense of the first word has long been recognized, and 'deaf' is the meaning rightly assigned to in Birch's Dictionary. One instance like the following is sufficient to settle the question: "He is not so deaf that he should not hear your voice." That the subject of these attributes is the Osiris is seen by reference to At, where instead of 'the Osiris' the deceased speaks in the first person, "I am dumb, I am deaf."

4. Sutu. This divine name occurs in the text of Amenemhait in the reign of Thothmes III. And I have noted another instance where the name is written. Dr. Birch called the papyrus Miss Brockelhurst's. It cannot, however, be the Ax of M. Naville, which does not contain the chapter. The disappearance of the God's name from all other documents is a fact.Chapter CXXXV: When the Moon Renews Itself

When the moon renews itself on the first day of the month, Osiris is enveloped in storm and rain. However, the fair Horus provides daily assistance, driving off the storm from Osiris N. Behold him coming: he is Ra on his journey, accompanied by the four Gods who oversee the upper region. Osiris arrives at his destined time and is brought to the light of day by his lines.

If this chapter is known, the deceased becomes a Chu of Might in the Netherworld, never dying a second time and eating by the side of Osiris. If known on earth, he will become like Thoth, worshipped by the living, and will not fall victim to a king's wrath or the fierce heat of Basil, advancing to a blissful old age.

Notes:
1. The phrase "Offerings of the Moment" appears to be an interpolated rubrical direction.
2. A king's wrath is an unstoppable impulse that carries everything before it.

Chapter CXXXVIa: Conveyance in the Bark of Ra

Lo, the Light rises in Cher-aba. He is born, he of the strong cord, his cable at an end, and his rudder taken in hand. I poise the divine machinery to raise the Bark to the cord above, allowing me to come forth into Heaven and be conveyed to Nut. I travel with Ra, like the Kaf, stopping the path at the Uarit of Nut, where Seb and Nut bewail their hearts.

Chapter CXXXVIb: Passage Through the Orbit of Flame

O bright flame behind Ra, dividing his Crown! The Bark of Ra fears the storm. You are bright and exalted. I come daily with Sek-hra from his exalted station to witness the process of Maat and the lion-forms. We rejoice: the great ones are jubilant, and the smaller ones are in bliss. I make my way at the prow of the Bark of Ra, shining like the Glorious ones, holding fast like a Lord of Maat. Here is the Cycle of the Gods and the Kite of Osiris. Grant that his father, the Lord of them, may judge in his favor. I poise the Balance of Maat and raise it to Tefnut for life. I repulse Apepi and heal the wounds he made. Let me pass through the midst of you. I am the Great one among the Gods, coming in the two Barks of the Lord of Sau, the Figure of the great saluter, who made the Flame. Let the fathers and their Apes make way for me to enter the Mount of Glory and pass through where the Great ones are. I see who is in his Bark and pass through the orbit of Flame behind the Lord of the Side-lock, over the serpents. Let me pass: I am the powerful one, the Lord of the powerful. I am the Sahu, the Lord of Maat, the creator of every Dawn. Place me among the followers of Ra, in the Garden of Peace of Ra. I am a God greater than you. Let me be numbered in the presence of the Divine Cycle when offerings are presented to me.

Notes:
1. The two chapters 136A and 136B are combined in later recensions. The ancient texts are obscure, and the more recent versions are equally difficult to understand. A strict literal and grammatical translation is necessary.
2. The word "Light" signifies a heavenly body, like the sun.
3. "He of the strong cord" is the subject of the verb "is born," a compound expression where the adjective precedes the substantive.
4. "His cable" refers to a passage in the Pyramid Texts about a similar voyage.
5. "Machinery" has been replaced by various conjectural emendations in later texts.
6. "The Kaf" refers to divinities in the form of apes, signifying "the hot one."
7. "Sek-hra" is a common reading, sometimes identified with Thoth.
8. "The Maat" refers to phenomena occurring in strict conformity with the laws of nature.
9. "Lion forms" are in a corrupt condition in some texts.
10. "Every Dawn" signifies the creator of every dawn.

Chapter CXXXVIIa: Kindling a Light for a Person

Oh Light! Let the Light be kindled for your Ka, O Osiris Chentamenta. Let the Light be kindled for the Night following the Day: the Eye of Horus rising at your temple, gathering upon your brow, granting you protection, and overthrowing your enemies. Undefiledly and successfully: The light is kindled for Osiris Unnefer with fresh vases and raiment.Chapter CXXXVIIb: Lighting a Lamp for a Person

The Eye of Horus appears, bringing light. The Eye of Horus appears, shining gloriously. Come forth, shining like Ra from the Mount of Glory, and end the opposition of Sutu. The one who raised him up and seized the light for him ends the troubles against you, like the Mount of Glory.

Notes:
1. The two oldest sources for this chapter are the Turin Todtenbuch and a late recension, one of the four tablets in the Museum of Marseilles, published by M. Naville, and the Berlin papyrus of Nechtuamon. The chapter published by M. Naville as 137A in his Todtenbuch is a revised and enlarged edition, not the original text. It concludes with a statement that it was discovered by Prince Hortatef in a secret chest in the temple of Unnut and brought away by royal carriages. These texts are also found in the tomb of Petamenemapt, with various additions, and have been used in the Ritual of Amnion, published by Dr. O. von Lemm. The ceremony of lighting the lamp for the dead is mentioned in the Siut inscriptions of Hapit'efae.
2. "Kindle" conveys the same notion as "strike a light" in the title of 137B. The Amnion Ritual uses "strike a light." Dr. von Lemm suggests a play on words implying both lighting a lamp and striking Sut.
3. "At your temple" in Abydos, Aa, and Petamenemapt.
4. "Rises up" in Marseilles; "opposition" in the Sallier Calendar. The sense is clarified in parallel passages.
5. "Prescription" and "her" refer to the Goddess Apit, depicted in hippopotamus form, lighting the lamp. Over her are the words "Apit, mistress of divine protections."

Chapter CXXXVIII: Entering Abydos

Oh all Gods in Abydos, each with their divine circle, who come to greet me: let me see my father Osiris. Let me be recognized as one who comes forth from his house. I am Horus, the Lord of Kamit, and the heir of Tesherit, which I have seized. I am invincible, with a potent eye against adversaries, avenging my father, and fierce at the drowning of my mother. I smite my adversaries and end their violence.

Notes:
1. "Each one and his" is necessary to bring out the meaning. Every God has a circle of associates.
2. The exact text here is doubtful. The word might mean a relative.
3. "Kamit" is Egypt; "Tesherit" is the land beyond Egypt.
4. "Drowning of his mother" refers to an incident in the career of the Goddess Isis.
5. A word of doubtful meaning follows. It must be connected with the preceding words.
6. "Seized" in the juridical sense of possession.
7. "Writs" is a reading from early papyri, which has disappeared in later ones. The Turin Todtenbuch has "with his two hands."
8. The chapter ends here in Pi and even sooner in later texts. The older papyri differ in the following words, which are corrupt and unintelligible.

Chapter CXXXIX: Identical with Chapter CXXIII

This completes Sir P. Le Page Renouf's translation of the Book of the Dead, as prepared for publication at the time of his death.

Chapter CXL: The Book Read on the Last Day of Mechir

A form rises, shining on the horizon. Atmu rises, pouring out his dew, and the bright one shines in the sky. The abode of the obelisk rejoices because they are complete. There are shouts of joy in the sanctuary, and loud cheering fills the Tuat. They fall before Atmu Harmachis. His Majesty orders the cycle of his followers to give praise to the Eye. My flesh is strengthened, and all my limbs are renewed as soon as the order comes from Ra. His glorious Eye rests on His Majesty in this hour of the night. When the fourth hour is accomplished, the world rejoices on the last day of Mechir, for the Majesty of the Eye is present with the Gods, and His Majesty rises as from the beginning, with the Eye on his head as Ra Atmu.

The eyes of Shu, Seb, Osiris, Suti, Horus, Menthu, Ptah, Raneheh, Thoth, Chati, Nai, Eternity, Necht, Mert, and the land, he who is born by himself. After the computation of the eye is made in the presence of this God, and when it is full and complete, all these Gods rejoice on that day. A festival is made for every God, and they say: Hail to you, praise from Ra, the boatmen tow his boat, Apepi is struck down. Hail to you, praise from Ra who causes the form of Chepera to exist; hail to you, praise from Ra, there is joy in him, his enemies are conquered; hail to you, praise from Ra, who has repelled the chiefs of the sons of rebellion. Acclamation to you and praise to Osiris N. Said on an eye of pure lapis-lazuli or mak stone, ornamented with gold; an offering is made before it of all things good and holy, when Ra puts it on his head on the last day of Mechir; another one is made of jasper, which a man will put on any of his limbs he likes.Chapter CXXXVIIb: Lighting a Lamp for a Person

The Eye of Horus appears, bringing light and shining gloriously. Come forth, shining like Ra from the Mount of Glory, and end the opposition of Sutu. The one who raised him up and seized the light for him ends the troubles against you, like the Mount of Glory.

Notes:
1. The two oldest sources for this chapter are the Turin Todtenbuch and a late recension, one of the four tablets in the Museum of Marseilles, published by M. Naville, and the Berlin papyrus of Nechtuamon. The chapter published by M. Naville as 137A in his Todtenbuch is a revised and enlarged edition, not the original text. It concludes with a statement that it was discovered by Prince Hortatef in a secret chest in the temple of Unnut and brought away by royal carriages. These texts are also found in the tomb of Petamenemapt, with various additions, and have been used in the Ritual of Amnion, published by Dr. O. von Lemm. The ceremony of lighting the lamp for the dead is mentioned in the Siut inscriptions of Hapit'efae.
2. "Kindle" conveys the same notion as "strike a light" in the title of 137B. The Amnion Ritual uses "strike a light." Dr. von Lemm suggests a play on words implying both lighting a lamp and striking Sut.
3. "At your temple" in Abydos, Aa, and Petamenemapt.
4. "Rises up" in Marseilles; "opposition" in the Sallier Calendar. The sense is clarified in parallel passages.
5. "Prescription" and "her" refer to the Goddess Apit, depicted in hippopotamus form, lighting the lamp. Over her are the words "Apit, mistress of divine protections."

Chapter CXXXVIII: Entering Abydos

Oh all Gods in Abydos, each with their divine circle, who come to greet me: let me see my father Osiris. Let me be recognized as one who comes forth from his house. I am Horus, the Lord of Kamit, and the heir of Tesherit, which I have seized. I am invincible, with a potent eye against adversaries, avenging my father, and fierce at the drowning of my mother. I smite my adversaries and end their violence.

Notes:
1. "Each one and his" is necessary to bring out the meaning. Every God has a circle of associates.
2. The exact text here is doubtful. The word might mean a relative.
3. "Kamit" is Egypt; "Tesherit" is the land beyond Egypt.
4. "Drowning of his mother" refers to an incident in the career of the Goddess Isis.
5. A word of doubtful meaning follows. It must be connected with the preceding words.
6. "Seized" in the juridical sense of possession.
7. "Writs" is a reading from early papyri, which has disappeared in later ones. The Turin Todtenbuch has "with his two hands."
8. The chapter ends here in Pi and even sooner in later texts. The older papyri differ in the following words, which are corrupt and unintelligible.

Chapter CXXXIX: Identical with Chapter CXXIII

This completes Sir P. Le Page Renouf's translation of the Book of the Dead, as prepared for publication at the time of his death.

Chapter CXL: The Book Read on the Last Day of Mechir

A form rises, shining on the horizon. Atmu rises, pouring out his dew, and the bright one shines in the sky. The abode of the obelisk rejoices because they are complete. There are shouts of joy in the sanctuary, and loud cheering fills the Tuat. They fall before Atmu Harmachis. His Majesty orders the cycle of his followers to give praise to the Eye. My flesh is strengthened, and all my limbs are renewed as soon as the order comes from Ra. His glorious Eye rests on His Majesty in this hour of the night. When the fourth hour is accomplished, the world rejoices on the last day of Mechir, for the Majesty of the Eye is present with the Gods, and His Majesty rises as from the beginning, with the Eye on his head as Ra Atmu.

The eyes of Shu, Seb, Osiris, Suti, Horus, Menthu, Ptah, Raneheh, Thoth, Chati, Nai, Eternity, Necht, Mert, and the land, he who is born by himself. After the computation of the eye is made in the presence of this God, and when it is full and complete, all these Gods rejoice on that day. A festival is made for every God, and they say: Hail to you, praise from Ra, the boatmen tow his boat, Apepi is struck down. Hail to you, praise from Ra who causes the form of Chepera to exist; hail to you, praise from Ra, there is joy in him, his enemies are conquered; hail to you, praise from Ra, who has repelled the chiefs of the sons of rebellion. Acclamation to you and praise to Osiris N. Said on an eye of pure lapis-lazuli or mak stone, ornamented with gold; an offering is made before it of all things good and holy, when Ra puts it on his head on the last day of Mechir; another one is made of jasper, which a man will put on any of his limbs he likes.

Chapter CXLI: The Book of the Arrival

The first gate. He whose face is overturned, who has many attributes, is the name of the occupant of the first gate. The adjuster, is the name of the warden thereof, and he with the loud voice the name of the herald.

The second gate. He who raises his face, is the name of the occupant of the second gate; he with the revolving face is the name of the warden thereof; the consuming one is the name of the herald.

The third gate. He who eats his own filth, is the name of the occupant. The watchful, is the name of the warden thereof; the consuming one is the name of the herald.The fourth gate is guarded by "He who opposes garrulity," with "The attentive one" as the warden and "The great one who drives back the crocodile" as the herald. The fifth gate's occupant is "He who lives on worms," with "The consuming flame" as the warden and "The horn which strikes the furious" as the herald. The sixth gate is occupied by "He who makes the loaves, with a thundering voice," with "He who shows his face" as the warden and "The stone knife which belongs to the sky" as the herald. The seventh gate's occupant is "He who takes possession of their knives," with "The high voice" as the warden and "He who drives back the enemies" as the herald.

These gates lead to Osiris, and those who guard them and herald the world's events to Osiris daily are known to Osiris N. He is born in Restau, where he receives the investiture in Pu, akin to Osiris's purification. N. leads the Gods on the horizon with the protectors of Osiris and is celebrated as a glorious one who performs the rites. N. celebrates the festival of the first day of the month and is the herald on the fifteenth day. N. carries the sacred flame to Thoth's hand at night and navigates in Ra's boat. N.'s attributes are those of Ra's boat, and he is greater and mightier than those on the roads of Maat. N. despises corruption and embodies Horus's attributes, the firstborn of Ra, fulfilling his will. N. is not fettered or driven away from Osiris's gates and is perfect, following Osiris Khent Amenta daily. His domains are in Sechet hotepu among those who know and perform sacred rites to Osiris. N. is on Thoth's side, bringing offerings, and Anubis ensures that N. receives his offerings without them being taken by captives. N. comes like Horus, adorning the horizon of heaven, and directs Ra's march towards the horizon's gates, bringing joy to the Gods.

The divine scent is upon Osiris, and the God with the lock will not reach him; the gatekeepers will not be hostile to him. N. is hidden inside the palace, in the sanctuary of the God, the lord of Tuat. N. reaches it after Hathor, gathers his hosts, brings Maat to Ra, and drives away the Mighty One, Apepi. N. pierces the steel firmament and repels the raging storm, giving life to Ra's seamen. N. carries offerings to the boat, ensuring a successful voyage. N. marches, and when he reaches it, his face is like the Great One, and his back like the lofty one. N. is the lord of the mighty, well-pleased on the horizon, valiant, striking down enemies, and making his way to Osiris.

This text is written in yellow ink on the sacred circle of Gods in Ra's boat, where offerings are made to revive the deceased and make him powerful among the Gods, ensuring he is not repulsed or driven back from the Tuat's pylons. Reading this text to the deceased's statue grants access to every hall in the books. Offerings include the haunch, head, heart, and hoof of a red bull, four vases of blood, scent vases, sixteen pointed white loaves, eight round loaves, eight chenfu loaves, eight hebennu loaves, eight casks of beer, eight vases of dry corn, four tanks of milk from a white cow, fresh herbs, olive oil, green eye paint, antimony, odoriferous oils, and burning incense. This is said while putting on a clay seal twice. Reading this book without being seen widens the deceased's steps in heaven, earth, and the Tuat, exalting him more than any ceremony.

Notes:
1. The title is from Papyrus Ax. The Turin text calls this chapter "the chapter of knowing the occupants of the seven gates."
2. A flame, as indicated by the determinative, is mentioned in chapter 147.
3. "Receives the saying" likely means receiving the right to say the following words: "I am one of them."
4. The word has various meanings, often corresponding to "nature" or used as a periphrase for an abstract adjective.
5. The God of the lock, another name for Apepi, an evil power to be driven away.
6. The steel firmament, often associated with storms and bad weather, possibly referring to the dark sky.
7. The books of Thoth, the divine writer.
8. The name of the book or page containing the offerings catalog.
9. Vignettes of chapter 144 depict the gates, warder, and herald; the occupant is not shown, unlike in chapter 147.
10. No definite order or rule in these figures, similar to the names, which vary in attribution.

Chapters CXLV and CXLVI: Knowing the pylons of Osiris's house in the Garden of Aarrti. The first pylon is named "The lady of trembling whose walls are high, the lady of destruction, who directs the words driving away the storm, forcing back the violent." The doorkeeper is "The brave." The second pylon is named...The second pylon is guarded by "The lady of heaven, mistress of the world, the consuming one, the lady of mankind, who counts the human beings." The doorkeeper's name is Meshept. 

The third pylon is "The lady of altars, rich in offerings, with whom all the Gods gather on the day they sail to Abydos." The doorkeeper's name is The Anointer.

The fourth pylon is "She who holds the knives, the mistress of the world, who destroys the enemies of the God whose heart is motionless, who gives advice, and is free from impurity." The doorkeeper's name is The Bull.

The fifth pylon is "The flame, the lady of the words of power, who gives joy to those who address their supplications to her, and whom no one on earth will come near." The doorkeeper's name is He Who Coerces the Rebels.

The sixth pylon is "The lady of light, who roars loud; whose length and breadth are unknown, and the like of whom never was found from the beginning. There are serpents on her, the number of which is unknown; they were born before the God whose heart is motionless." The doorkeeper's name is The Consort.

The seventh pylon is "The shroud which enwraps the dead; the monster who seeks to hide the body." The doorkeeper's name is Akesti.

The eighth pylon is "The burning flame whose fire is never quenched; she who is provided with burning heat, who sends forth her hand, and slaughters without mercy. Nobody goes near her for fear of being hurt." The doorkeeper's name is He Who Protects His Body.

The ninth pylon is "The foremost, the Mighty One, the joyous who gives birth to her lord; whose circumference is 350 measures; she who shines like southern emerald, who raises Besu, and encourages the dead, she who provides her lord with offerings every day."

The tenth pylon is "She with a loud voice; who shouts curses to those who make supplications to her; the very brave, the dreadful, who does not destroy what is within her." The doorkeeper's name is He Who Embraces the Great God.

The eleventh pylon is "She who renews her knives, who consumes her enemies, the mistress of all pylons, to whom acclamations are given in the daytime and in the twilight. She will prepare the enwrapping of the dead."

The twelfth pylon is "She who addresses her world and destroys those who come through the morning heat, the lady of brightness, who listens to the words of her lord every day. She will prepare the enwrapping of the dead."

The thirteenth pylon is "Isis extends her two hands upon her; she lightens the Nile in its hidden abode. She will prepare the enwrapping of the dead."

The fourteenth pylon is "The lady of fear, who dances on the impure, to whom the Haker festival is celebrated on the day of the hearing of yells. She will prepare the enwrapping of the dead."

The fifteenth pylon is "The evil one, with red hair and eyes, who comes out at night, who binds her enemy all around, who puts her hands over the God whose heart is motionless, in his hour of danger, who goes and comes. She will prepare the enwrapping of the dead."

The sixteenth pylon is "The terrible, the lady of the morning dew, who throws out her burning heat, and sprinkles her sparks of fire over her enemies when she appears. She who creates the mysteries of the earth. She will prepare the enwrapping of the dead."

The seventeenth pylon is "She who revels in blood; Aahit, the lady of the unusual plants. She will prepare the enwrapping of the dead."

The eighteenth pylon is "She who likes fire, who washes her knives, who loves cutting heads, the welcome one, the lady of the palace, who slays her enemies in the evening. She will prepare the enwrapping of the dead."

The nineteenth pylon is "She who directs the morning light in her time, and observes the midday heat, the lady of the books written by Thoth himself. She will prepare the enwrapping of the dead."

The twentieth pylon is "She who is within the cavern of her lord, who covers her name, and hides what she creates, who takes possession of hearts, which she swallows. She will prepare the enwrapping of the dead."

The twenty-first pylon is "She who cuts the stone by her word, and sacrifices him on whom her flames fall. She follows the hidden counsels."

Notes:
- Chapters 145 and 146 are two versions of the same text, describing the arrival of the deceased at the house of Osiris.
- The term "pylon" is used to describe these structures, but they are more like cells, each with an inhabitant.
- There are various versions of these chapters, with the oldest being found in several papyri.
- The text describes the names of the pylons and their doorkeepers, as well as the purifications and anointments the deceased undergoes.
- The deceased is supposed to wear a different garment at each pylon, provided by the pylon itself.
- Chapters 145 and 146 are among the most incorrect texts of the Book of the Dead, and there is a large measure of conjecture in any attempt to translate them.The second gate is guarded by "He Who Shows His Face." The gatekeeper is "He with a Revolving Face," and the herald is "The Consumer." When approaching this gate, the deceased says: "I am Osiris. I am the divine mummy. What I say happens. I will not be turned away. The walls of burning coals show the way in Restau. I have soothed Osiris's pain and supported him. I have made my way to the light of Osiris."

The third gate is guarded by "He Who Eats His Own Filth." The gatekeeper is "The Watchful," and the herald is "The Great One." When approaching this gate, the deceased says: "I am the secret stream, the judge of Rehui. I have come to remove all evil from Osiris. I am girdled and come forth with the double crown. I secured my place in Abydos and opened my path in Restau. I have soothed Osiris's pain and made my way when he shines at Restau."

The fourth gate is guarded by "He Who Opposes Garrulity." The gatekeeper is "The Attentive One," and the herald is "He Who Drives Back the Crocodile." When approaching this gate, the deceased says: "I am the bull, the son of the Kite of Osiris. His father, the Fiery One, sat in judgment. I poised the balance for him. Life has been brought to me. I live forever. I have made my way. I am the son of Osiris, I live forever."

The fifth gate is guarded by "He Who Lives on Worms." The gatekeeper is "The Consuming Flame," and the herald is "The Bow Which Strikes the Furious." When approaching this gate, the deceased says: "I have brought the two jaws of Restau. I have brought the books from Annu and added up his hosts. I have repulsed Apepi and healed the wounds he made. I made my way through you. I am the great one among the Gods. I purified Osiris and restored him as victor. I joined his bones and put together his limbs."

The sixth gate is guarded by "He Who Makes the Loaves, with a Thundering Voice." The gatekeeper is "He Who Shows His Face," and the herald is "The Stolen Knife Which Belongs to the Sky." When approaching this gate, the deceased says: "I come every day, I go. I was created by Anubis, I am the lord of the diadem. I ignore the magic words. I avenge Maat, I avenge his eye. I gave his eye to Osiris himself. I have made my way."

The seventh gate is guarded by "He Who Takes Possession of Their Knives." The gatekeeper is "He with a High Voice," and the herald is "He Who Drives Back the Enemies." When approaching this gate, the deceased says: "I have come to you, Osiris. Pure are your effluxes. You go around and see the sky with Ra. You see mankind, you the only one. You address Ra in the Sektit boat of the sky when he goes around the horizon. I say what I wish, my mummy is mighty. What I say happens like what he says. I will not be turned away from you. I have made my way."

When the deceased arrives at the pylons, he is not turned away or repulsed from Osiris. He is given a place among the glorious ones, the most excellent of them, so that he may have dominion over the first followers of Osiris. Every deceased to whom this chapter is read is like the lord of eternity, he is of one substance with Osiris, and in no place does he have to encounter a great fight.

Chapter 147 is very similar to Chapter 144, but more developed. It also refers to the seven gates. Whenever the deceased approaches one of the gates, he has to say the name of the doorkeeper, which is also the name of the gate itself, as well as the name of the warder and the herald. The deceased also has to address the gate to open it and pass through. The words he utters are found in Chapters 117, 119, and 136B. The two first have nearly the same title, "The Arrival at Restau, near Abydos." If the various parts of the Book of the Dead did not originate in the same place, we can assert that these chapters, as well as those of the gates and the pylons, come from Abydos. The Papyrus of Ani is more complete for Chapter 147 than the Leyden text, which is published in my edition. Therefore, this chapter has been translated from Ani, using the Leyden text whenever Ani is too corrupt.

Chapter 148: Giving sustenance to the deceased in the Netherworld and delivering him from all evil things.

Hail to you who shines as a living soul and appears on the horizon. N, who is in the boat, knows you; he knows your name and the names of the seven cows and their bull. They give bread and drink to the glorified soul. You who give sustenance to the inhabitants of the West, give bread and drink to the soul of N. Grant that he may be your follower and be between your thighs.

(Then follow the names of the seven cows.)

The house of the ka, of the inviolate God,
The storm of the sky, which raises the Gods,
The hidden one in her dwelling,
Chebt, the mummified form of the God,
The greatly beloved, with red hair,
The abundant in life, the veiled one,
She who is powerful in her works, or on her pedestal,
The bull of the Netherworld.

(Then the deceased calls on the four rudders of the sky, the four cardinal points.)

Hail! Divine form, the good one, the good rudder of the Northern sky.
Hail! You who go around and pilot the double earth, the good rudder of the Western sky.
Hail! The shining one, who dwells in the house of the devouring monsters, the good rudder of the Eastern sky.
Hail! The inner one who dwells in the house of the red ones, the good rudder of the Southern sky.

Give bread and drink, oxen, geese, all things good and pure to N. Give him sustenance, give him joy, may he rest on the earth, and may he be victorious on the horizon of Annu, in the Tuat, in the sky, and on the earth, eternally. Ye fathers and mothers, Gods of the sky and the Netherworld, deliver N from all things pernicious and evil, from all harm and evil, from the cruel huntsman and his swords, and from all evil things; and order what is to be done to him by the men, the glorious ones, and the dead, in this day, in this night, in this month, and in this year.

Said by a man when Ra is put before these Gods, painted in green, and standing on a wooden board, and when they give him the offerings and sustenance which is before them, bread and drink, geese, and frankincense, and when they present mortuary gifts to the deceased before Ra. The book called "Giving Sustenance to a Deceased in the Netherworld" delivers a man from all evil things. You shall not read it to any other man than yourself. He to whom this has been read, Ra is his steersman and his protecting power, he will not be attacked by his enemies in the Netherworld, in the sky, on the earth, and in every place he goes, for the book "Giving Sustenance to the Deceased" has its effect regularly.Hatshepsu at Der el Bahari, by Hathor. Several papyri here have the rubric of 30B, with the name of Mycerinus. The rubric translated here is taken from the papyrus of N^i/. Lepsius calls 148c the vignettes belonging to this chapter. In a columned hall stands Osiris, and behind him are the cows, the rudders, and the four Gods of the cardinal points. Sometimes Osiris is left out. In the papyrus of Ani, the God has his hair painted green and stands on a green base.

Chapter 149: The First Domain
In this domain of the Amenta, they live on bread made from the plant tej. Remove your head dress in my presence, for I am the great one among you, the one who joins his bones and firmly establishes his limbs. Ahi, the lord of hearts, came to me, joined my bones, and fixed the diadem of Tmu on me, fastening the head of Nehebkau and establishing my balance. I am lord among the Gods, I am Amsi the builder.

The Second Domain
I am the great proprietor in the garden of Aarru. This garden has steel walls, its wheat is seven cubits high, the ears are two cubits, and the stalks five cubits. The glorified ones, each seven cubits tall, reap them in the presence of Harmachis. I know the inner gate of the garden of Aarru, from which Ra emerges in the East of the sky. The South is by the lake of Cha ru, and the North by the stream of Reu. Ra sails with favoring gales. I am the Teller in the divine ship; I am the unresting navigator in the Bark of Ra. I know the two sycamores of emerald, between which Ra emerges as he advances over what Tmu has lifted up (the firmament) to the Eastern gates of the sky. I know this garden of Aarru of Ra, where the wheat is seven cubits high, the ears are two cubits, and the stalks five cubits. The barley is seven cubits. The glorified ones, each nine cubits tall, reap them in the presence of the powers of the East.

The Third Domain
This domain of the glorious ones is impassable and contains a consuming fire. The faces of the glorious ones look down; make straight your ways and purify your abodes as ordered by Osiris the eternal one. I am the lord of the red crown on the head of the shining one, who gives life to mankind from the heat of his mouth and delivers Ra from Apepi.

The Fourth Domain
This great and lofty mountain of the Netherworld ends at the highest point of the sky. It is three hundred measures long and ten wide. A snake named "He with sharp knives" lives here, seventy cubits in his windings, living by slaughtering the glorious ones and the damned in the Netherworld. I stand on your wall, directing my navigation. I see the way towards you. I gather myself together. I am the man who puts a veil on your head, and I am uninjured. I am the great magician; your eyes have been given to me, and I am glorified through them. Who is he who goes on his belly? Your strength is on your mountain; behold, I march towards it, and your strength is in my hand. I am he who lifts the strength. I have come and taken away the serpents of Ra when he rests with me at eventide. I go around the sky; you are in your valley, as ordered to you before.

The Fifth Domain
This domain of the glorious ones is open to no one. The glorious ones in it have thighs of seven cubits and live on the shades of the motionless. Open the ways to me, that I may appear before you and reach the good Amenta, as ordered by Osiris, the glorious one, the lord of all the glorified. I live off your glory, observing the first day of the month and the half-month on the fifteenth day. I have gone around with the eye of Horus in my power, following Thoth. Any God or damned who opens his devouring mouth against me on this day is struck down on the block.

The Sixth Domain
O Amemhet, sacred more than the hidden Gods and the glorious ones, dreadful to the Gods. The God in it is called Sechez-at. Hail to you, Amemhet. I have come to see the Gods within you. Show your faces and remove your head-dresses in my presence. I have come to make your bread. Sechez-at will not be stronger than I; the slaughterers will not come behind me, the impure ones will not come behind me. I live upon your offerings.

The Seventh Domain
This Ases is too remote to be seen; its heat is that of blazing fire. A serpent named Rerek lives here, with a backbone of seven cubits, living on glorious ones and destroying their glory. Get behind me, Rerek, who is in Ases, who bites with his mouth and paralyzes with his eyes. Your teeth are torn away, your venom is powerless. You shall not come towards me; your venom will not penetrate me. Your poison is fallen and thrown down, and your lips are in a hole. The white serpent has struck his ka, and his ka has struck the white serpent. I shall be protected. His head was cut off by the lynx.

The Eighth Domain
This Hahotep, the very great, has a stream from which nobody takes water for fear of its roaring. The God named the lofty one keeps watch over it so that nobody may come near it. I am the vulture on the stream without end. I brought the things of the world to Tmu when the sailors of Ra are abundantly provided. I have given my strength to the lords of the shrines and the awe I inspire to the lord of all things. I shall not be taken to the block. The pleasure they take in me will not be destroyed. I am the guide on the northern horizon.

The Ninth Domain
This Akset is hidden to the Gods, and the glorious ones are afraid to know its name. No one goes out who goes into it, except this venerable God who inspires fear in the Gods and terror in the glorious ones. Its opening is of fire, and its wind destroys the nostrils. He made it such for his followers so they may not breathe its wind, except this venerable God who comes out of his egg. Hail to you, venerable God, who comes out of his egg. I have come to you to be in your following. I go out of and come into Akset. Open the doors to me, that I may inhale its wind and take the offerings within it.

The Tenth Domain
This city of the Kahu Gods takes hold of the glorious ones and gains mastery over the shades they see with their eyes, who have no connection with the earth. O you who are in your domain, throw yourselves on your bellies, that I may pass near you. My glorious nature will not be taken from me. No one will gain mastery over my shade, for I am the divine hawk rubbed with anti and anointed with incense. Libations have been offered to me; Isis is before me, Nephthys is behind me. The way has been pointed to me by Nau, the bull of Nut and Nehebkau. I have come to you, Gods; deliver me and glorify me with eternal glory.

The Eleventh Domain
This city in the Netherworld, this cavity, masters the glorious ones. No one goes out of those who went into it, from the dread of the appearance of him who is in it. He who sees the God in it, face to face, dies there from his blows, except the Gods who are there and hidden to the glorious ones. O this Atu in the Netherworld. Grant that I may reach them; I am the great magician with his knife; I am issued of Set. I stand on my feet forever. I rise, and I am mighty through this eye of Horus; my heart is raised after it has fallen low. I am glorious in heaven, and I am mighty on earth. I fly like Horus, I cackle like the divine goose. It was given to me to alight near the stream of the lake; I stand near it, I sit near it, I eat of the food in Sechit Hotepit, I go down to the islands of the wandering stars. The doors of the Maati are open to me, and the gates of the upper waters are unbolted to me. I raise my ladder up to the sky to see the Gods. I am one of them, I speak like the divine goose, and I listen to the Gods. I talk aloud, I repeat the words of Sothis.

The Twelfth Domain
This domain of Unt, within Restau, has the heat of fire. No God goes down into it, and the glorious ones do not gather into it, for the four snakes would destroy their names. O this domain of Unt! I am the great among the glorious ones within. I am among the wandering stars. I am not destroyed; my name is not destroyed. Come, divine scent, say the Gods who are in the domain of Unt. I am with you, I live with you, Gods who are within the domain of Unt. You love me more than your Gods. I am with you forever, in the presence of the followers of the great God.

The Thirteenth Domain
This domain of water, which none of the glorious ones can possess, has water of fire, a burning stream, and blazing flame, so they may not drink its water to quench their thirst. The Gods and the glorious ones look at its water from afar, they do not quench their thirst, and their hearts are not set at rest because they may not go near it.The Fourteenth Domain
This domain, Cher-aba, directs the Nile towards Tattu and causes it to flow from Kokekmu. It offers gifts to the dead and the glorious ones. A serpent from the two wells at Elephantine guards the water gate and travels with the Nile, stopping at Cher-aba's stream. Gods of Cher-aba, open your ponds and lakes to me so I may drink, rest, and be nourished. I am the great God in Cher-aba, filled with the vital essence of Osiris. I will not be deprived of it.

Notes
This chapter is frequently found at the end of Theban papyri, detailing the various domains the deceased must reach to enjoy special privileges. The vignettes often depict the domain's layout and colors, typically green or light yellow. Renouf translates "domain" as "residence" or "habitation," indicating an enclosed space with inhabitants. The deceased addresses the domain and its inhabitants without transition.

1. The second domain is the horizon, with the God Harmachis.
2. The third domain is "that of the glorious ones."
3. The moon is mentioned as "on the face of the sun and moon."
4. The deceased, as a magician, can neutralize the serpent's paralyzing eyes.
5. Renouf translates "serpent" or "worms" in different contexts.
6. Secher-remn means "he who knocks down the worm or fishes."
7. The ka and serpent have killed each other.
8. The lynx, or cat, is depicted cutting off the serpent's head.
9. A chapter on the sarcophagus of Amam describes taking the form of a vulture or goose.
10. The ninth domain, Akset, is shaped like a vase touched by a crocodile named Maatetf.
11. Akset was designed to prevent followers from breathing its destructive wind.
12. The tenth domain is at the mouth of the stream.
13. Some words are unclear and untranslated.
14. Destroying a name means complete destruction of the person.
15. Cher-aba is preferred over Cher-aha by some Egyptologists.
16. Kokekmu is believed to be the origin of the rocks mentioned by Herodotus.

Chapter 151
This chapter includes vignettes accompanying Chapter 149, often found at the end of many papyri. It describes fifteen domains, with the fifth divided into two. Four serpents at the corners represent the cardinal points. The domains are named in the following order:

1. The good Amenta, where Gods live on loaves.
2. The garden of Aarru, with the God Ra.
3. The domain of the glorious ones.
4. The high and lofty mountain.
5. The basin with blazing fire, guarded by the bearer of altars.
6. Amemhet, with the God who knocks down fishes.
7. Asset.
8. Hasert, with the bearer of heaven.
9. Akset, with the God Maatetf.
10. The face of the Kahu Gods.
