11. Aat, with the God Sothis.
12. The domain of Unt, with the destroyer of souls.
13. The surface of the water, with the mighty power.
14. The domain of Cher-aba, with the God Nile.

Words of Anubis
Your right eye is in the Sektit boat, your left eye in the Atit boat. Your eyebrows are with Anubis, fingers with Thoth, and locks with Ptah Sokaris. They prepare a good path for you and defeat your enemies.

Words of Isis
I come as your protector, with the breath of Tmu. I strengthen your throat and make you like a God, placing your enemies under your feet.

Words of Nephthys
I circle my brother Osiris as your protector, always behind you, hearing Ra and justifying you before the Gods. Arise, justified by all that has been done for you. Ptah has defeated your enemies; you are Horus, son of Hathor. Your head will remain with you forever.

Words of the Northern Wall Figure
I will not let anyone enchain or bind you. I am here to protect you.

Words of the Western Wall Tat
Come quickly and turn away Kep-her's steps. Bring light to his hidden abode. I am behind Tat, protecting you on the day of repelling slaughter.

Words of the Southern Wall Flame
I spread sand around the hidden abode, repelling aggressors and illuminating the mountain. I protect you.

Words of Anubis in Ta-Tsert
I watch over your head. Awake on the mountain, your wrath averted. I protect you.

Words of the Soul Figures
The living soul of N. worships the sun at dawn and Ra at sunset.

Words of the Statuettes
O statuette, if called to work in the Netherworld, I am ready to plant fields, water soil, and move sand.

Words of the Four Cardinal Points Genii
Kebehsenuf: I protect you, join your bones, and strengthen your limbs.
Hapi: I revive your head and limbs, defeat your enemies, and give you your head forever.
Tuamautef: I am Horus, rescuing my father from evildoers.
Emsta: I protect you and ensure your house prospers, as commanded by Ptah and Ra.

Notes
Chapter 151 begins a series of texts found on funeral chamber walls, mummy cloth, or amulets, continuing to Chapter 160. Chapter 151 is more pictorial, representing the funeral chamber.In the middle of the chamber, under a canopy, lies the mummy, with Anubis placing his hands on it. Beneath the bed is a bird with a human head, symbolizing the soul of the deceased. Anubis is likely a priest or family member wearing a jackal's head, reciting words attributed to the God. At the foot of the bed stand the Goddesses Isis and Nephthys. Each of the four walls has a niche for an amulet, as seen in the four oriented steles of Marseilles. The North wall features a human figure, the South a flame, the East a jackal, and the West a Tat. The chamber also contains four canopic vases with the Gods of the cardinal points, each delivering their own words. Additionally, there are statuettes called shabti or ushabti, helpers of the deceased in the afterlife. In the London papyrus, one statuette has the usual appearance, while another has the head of Anubis. The soul of the deceased is believed to be in the chamber, worshipping the rising and setting sun. Few papyri have this chapter as complete as the London version, which serves as the standard for text and vignettes. The Turin version is much shorter. The papyrus of Ani contains texts for the four walls with rubrics similar to those in Marseilles, forming a special chapter joined to Chapter 137a, titled "What is done secretly in the Tuat, the mysteries of the Tuat, the introduction into the mysteries of the Netherworld." To aid understanding, the words spoken by various figures are lettered.

1. Renouf would have translated "thy eyebrows are those of Anubis," but the following chapter shows it should be "with Anubis," meaning under his protection.
2. The rubrics state the figure is made of palm wood and is seven fingers high.
3. The rubric for the Tat says it is made of crystal with gold branches, wrapped in fine linen. Another chapter (Chapter 155) describes a different Tat placed on the deceased's neck.
4. The flame is described as a torch made of reeds.
5. The Anubis figure is made of clay.
6. Words are engraved on the funerary statuettes, an abridged form of Chapter 6, for which Renouf's translation is used.

Chapter CLII: The Chapter of Building a House on Earth
Seb rejoices as N. is set in motion with his vital power, giving men and Gods their creative strength. There is cheering when Seshait approaches Seb, and Anubis commands N. to build a house on earth with foundations like On and a circuit like Cher-aba. The God of the sanctuary should reside within. Osiris tells the Gods to come quickly and see the house built for the glorified, who comes every day. They should hold him in awe and give him praise. Osiris brings cattle, the south wind brings grain, and the north wind brings barley. Osiris is exalted, surrounded by applause from men, Gods, and Chus.

Chapter CLIIIa: The Chapter of Coming Out of the Net
The deceased addresses the mighty-hearted one who spreads his net and enters the earth, declaring that the fishermen will not catch him in their net or carry him away. He will escape the net's meshes and shine like Hunnu (Sokaris) and Sebak. He knows the fork, the stake, and the names of the net's components, all linked to divine figures. The deceased will shine like Horus, govern the land, and be introduced into the house of the Prince. He comes as a fisher, equipped with a fork, blade, and knife, ready to entangle in his net. He knows the names of the net's parts and the fishermen, who are ancestors of Ra and Seb. The deceased declares that he will not be caught in the net, asserting his divine knowledge and power.You won't trap me in your net, which catches the weak and those in the earth. I know the net, its frame above, and its weights below. I come with my stake, point, and blade in hand. I arrive to bind and place it. My knife is sharpened and ready. The stake in my hand is the thigh of Nemu; the fork is the fingers of Sokaris; the point is the claws of Isis; the blade is the knife of Nemu. I come, sit in Ra's boat, and sail on the celestial lakes. I hear the Gods' words, do as they do, praise them, and live as they live. N. appears on the ladder made by his father Ra, with Horus and Sut holding him.

Notes:
In the Theban version, the Chapter of the Net is split into two parts, 153A and 153B, with different titles and illustrations. 153A is about escaping the net, depicted as a clap-net for waterfowl. 153B is about escaping fish catchers, shown with a drag-net containing fish, drawn by apes. Originally, one chapter might have been for fowlers and the other for fishermen, but they are now combined in the best-preserved texts. The text of 153A is corrupt and varies significantly between documents, indicating a loss of understanding. The Turin text only contains 153A, much shorter, followed by a rubric absent in the Theban version. The translation is based on three main documents. The vignette in the Louvre papyrus shows a clap-net drawn by four men, with the deceased holding two instruments mentioned in the text. In the London papyrus, the deceased is seen drawing the net's rope.

Among the dangers for the deceased is being caught in a net by hidden spirits, treated like waterfowl or fish. But he escapes because he knows the mystical names of the fowlers, fishermen, and the net's parts, giving him magical power. The instrument in the deceased's hand, though determinative of wood, may be a general weapon, like a bident for spearing fish. The stake or peg in the London vignette is a dagger, with a pointed head and blade. Nemu might be a local name for Horus. The God in lion form is the Sphinx. The late recension of Chapter 153 ends here, followed by a rubric: Said on a figure of the deceased in a boat, with the Ssktit boat on the right and the Atit boat on the left. Offerings of cakes, beer, and good things are made on Osiris's birth day. The one who receives these will live forever and not die again.

The word "marked" means to mark an object for religious purposes or as property. Fishes are marked on the tail. There is an opposition between "those who are" and "those who are not," meaning future ones. The negative often expresses the future, what is to come. An official of the 12th dynasty says the king made him commissioner of present and future work. Isis issues directions for what is and what will be. The first beings or creatures are sometimes mentioned before the Gods.

Chapter CLIIIb: Escaping from Fish Catchers
O snarers, fowlers, fishers, sons of their fathers, do you know what I know? The name of the great net is the embracer. The name of its cordage is the bonds of Isis. The name of its stake is the thigh of Tmu. The name of the fork is the finger of Nemu. The name of its point is the nail of Ptah. The name of its blade is the knife of Isis. The name of its weight is the iron in the sky. The name of its flowers is the feathers of the hawk. The name of the fisherman is the cynocephalus. The name of the ground, where its limits are, is the house of the moon. The name of the one who fishes there is the great prince who sits on the east of the sky. I am Ra, who proceeds from Nu, and my soul is divine. I produce food but reject what is wrong. I am Osiris, possessor of Maat, and I live by it daily. I am eternal, like the bull, feared by the Gods in my name of the eternal one. I am self-originating with Nu, in my name of Chepera, born daily. I am the lord of Daylight, shining like Ra, who gives me life in his risings in the East. I come to heaven, take my place in the East. The children of the great God nourish me with sacred offerings. I eat and ease myself like Shu. The king of Egypt (Osiris) is present. Khonsu and Thoth's laws are within me, imparting warmth to the heavenly host.

Notes:
This chapter is found in two papyri: Paris, III, 93, and the Papyrus of Nu, both with some errors. The first part is a list of the net's parts, similar to 153A. The vignette shows a drag-net drawn by three dog-headed apes. The old participial form means "do you know well?" or "are you certain to know?" The word likely means papyrus flowers tied to the net. The discrepancies between texts are significant, making translation difficult. The following lines are an abridged version of Chapter 85, using Renouf's translation. The bull of Amenta, Osiris, is mentioned in the first chapter.Chapter CLIV: The Chapter of Preventing the Body from Decaying in the Underworld

Greetings, my father Osiris. I have come to embalm you. Embalm this body of mine, for I am perfect like my father Chepera, who does not know decay. Come, take hold of my breath of life, lord of breath, exalted above all. Revive me, build me up, lord of the funeral chest. Allow me to enter the land of eternity, as you do when you are with your father Tmu, whose body never decays. I have not done what you hate; I follow the commands that your ka loves. I have not transgressed them. I have been saved, being your follower, O Tmu, from the decay that affects every God, Goddess, animal, and creeping thing. After their souls depart, they die and decay; their bones rot, their flesh becomes a foul liquid, and they turn into a mass of worms. But as for me, there are no worms. Whoever loses the eye of Shu among all beings becomes powerless. I cause them to crawl before me; they recognize me and fear me. All beings are alike dead among animals, birds, fish, snakes, and worms; their life is like death. Let there be no food for the worms. Let them not come to me when they are born. I shall not be handed over to the destroyer who corrupts and dismembers bodies. He who follows his commands lives, but I have not been delivered into his hands, for I am under your command, lord of the Gods. Greetings, my father Osiris! Your limbs are lasting; you do not know decay. There are no worms with you; you are not repugnant, you do not stink, you do not rot, you do not become worms. I am Chepera; my limbs are lasting forever. I do not know decay. I do not rot, I do not putrefy, I do not become worms. I do not lose the eye of Shu. I am, I am, I live, I live, I grow, I grow, and when I awake in peace, I shall not be in decay. I shall not be destroyed in my bandages. I shall be free of pestilence; my eye will not be corrupted, my skin will not disappear. My ear will not be deaf, my head will not be taken from my neck, my tongue will not be torn away, my hair will not be cut off, my eyebrows will not be shaved off. No grievous harm shall come upon me; my body is firm and shall not be destroyed. It shall not perish in this earth forever.

Notes:
This chapter is rarely found in papyri; it was written on the wrappings and bandages of the dead, such as on the funeral cloth of King Thothmes III, where it is incomplete. This chapter is interesting as it shows how repulsive the idea of decay was to the Egyptians, which is described here in very realistic terms. This is one reason why they valued mummification so highly. Parts of this chapter are very obscure. The translation is based on the text on the mummy cloth of Thothmes III, supplemented by the Papyrus of Nu. The only vignette we have is from the Turin Papyrus, showing a mummy lying on a bed, illuminated by the rays of the sun.

Chapter CLV: The Chapter of the Tat of Gold

Here is your backbone, still-heart! Here is your spine, still-heart! Put it close to you. I have given you the water you need. Here it is. I have brought you the Tat, which makes your heart rejoice. Said on a Tat of gold inlaid into sycamore wood and dipped into the juice of ankhamu. If it is put on the neck of this deceased, he arrives at the doors of the Tuat and comes forth by day, even if he is silent. The Tat is placed on the first day of the year, as is done for the followers of Osiris.

Notes:
After the interruption due to Chapters 153 and 154, we return to the series started by Chapter 151, describing the chamber where the mummy is placed and the funeral equipment of the deceased, including his amulets and ornaments. The Louvre papyrus III, 93 (Pb), combines several of these chapters into one, titled "The Description of the Hidden Things of the Tuat," with a vignette showing three figures from Chapter 151: the statuette, the torch or flame, and Anubis, along with two Tat of different materials, one for the wall and one for the neck of the deceased, and a buckle. The vignette of Chapter 155 shows a Tat of gold. The various versions of the chapter differ mainly in the rubric. I followed the papyrus of Nebseni (Aa), filling in gaps from other texts.

Chapter CLVI: The Chapter of the Buckle of Carnelian

The blood of Isis, the virtue of Isis; the magic power of Isis, the magic power of the Eye protect this Great one; they prevent any harm from coming to him. This chapter is said on a buckle of carnelian dipped into the juice of ankhamu, inlaid into sycamore wood, and placed on the neck of the deceased. Whoever has this chapter read to him is protected by the virtue of Isis: Horus, the son of Isis, rejoices in seeing him, and no path is barred to him, unfailingly.

Notes:
M. Maspero, who studied this chapter in detail, has shown that there are several versions. This, likely the oldest, is taken from the papyrus of Nebseni, with a few additions from texts of the same date. The protective power of the buckle is shown in the vignette of Chapter 93, where a buckle with human hands grasps the deceased by the left arm, preventing him from moving towards the East.

Chapter CLVII: The Chapter of the Vulture of Gold

Isis has arrived; she hovers over the dwellings, searching all the hidden abodes of Horus when he emerges from the Northern marshes, knocking down those with evil faces. She causes him to join the Bark and grants him sovereignty over the...Chapter CLVIII: The Chapter of the Gold Collar

O my father! My brother! My mother Isis! I am unveiled and I am seen. I am one of the unveiled ones who see Seb. This is said on a gold collar, on which this chapter is written, and placed on the neck of the deceased on the day of burial.

Chapter CLIX: The Chapter of the Green Felspar Column

O you who come out every day in the divine house, she who has a big voice, who goes around, she takes hold of the potent formulae of her father, the mummy which is on the bull. She is Renent. This is said on a column of green felspar, on which this chapter is written, and placed on the neck of the deceased.

Notes:
The vignette of this chapter and the next shows a miniature column or tent-pole with a papyrus capital and papyrus leaves at the base. This chapter is taken from the Turin text; parts of it are quite unintelligible. The mineral mentioned has not yet been determined. Brugsch calls it "Opal," Lepsius thought its color was blue, Dr. Budge translates it as "mother-of-emerald," and Renouf's translation is "green felspar."

Chapter CLX: Giving the Column of Green Felspar

I am the column of green felspar, which cannot be crushed, and which is raised by the hand of Thoth. Injury is an abomination for it. If it is safe, I am safe; if it is not injured, I am not injured; if it receives no cut, I receive no cut. Said by Thoth: arise, come in peace, lord of Heliopolis, lord who resides at Pu. When Shu has arrived, he found the stone at Shenemu, as its name is neshem. The deceased makes his abode in the enclosure of the great God, while Tmu resides in his dwelling; his limbs will never be crushed.

Notes:
For Chapter 160, we have a text from London, 9900 (Aa); it is not complete, but the gaps can easily be filled from the Papyrus Busca. The vignette of Aa represents Thoth bringing the column, enclosed in a box or a casket. The symbolic expressions of this chapter mean that the neshem, of which the column is made, is a very hard stone, proof against any injury. The power of the amulet consists in making the body of the deceased as hard as neshem.

Chapter CLXI: The Chapter of Unfastening the Opening in the Sky

Thoth does it so that it may be finished when he opens the sky with Aten. Ra is living, the tortoise is dead. The body has been offered in the earth; the bones have been offered of N. [The West wind of Isis]. Ra is living, the tortoise is dead. It is safe that is in the funeral chest of N. [The East wind of Nephthys.] Ra is living, the tortoise is dead, the limbs are well wrapped up. Kebehsenef is to keep watch over them for N. [The North wind of Osiris.] Ra is living, the tortoise is dead. His wrappings have been opened; they reveal his figure. [The South wind of Ra.] Everybody who has these figures on his coffin, the four openings of the sky are open to him; one in the North, it is the wind of Osiris; one in the South, it is the wind of Aah (the moon); one in the West, it is the wind of Isis; one in the East, it is the wind of Nephthys. Every one of these winds, which are at his entrance when he wants it, breathes into his nostrils. Let no one outside know it, it is a mystery which is not known to the common people. Do not reveal it to anyone, may he be thy father or thy son, except thyself. It is a real mystery, and every one of these things is unknown to all men.

Notes:
This chapter is so short in the old recension (Paris, III, 93) that it could hardly be understood without the rubric of the Turin text. The four Thoths, each of whom opens a door, are the four winds, coming from the four cardinal points. We have already learned from Chapter 59 that it is one of the privileges of the deceased to have the command of the four winds.

Chapter CLXII: Chapter of Causing a Flame to Arise Under the Head of the Deceased

Hail to thee, thou lion, thou mighty one, with high plumes, the lord of the double crown, who waves the flail, thou art the lord of the phallus, thou art vigorous when the morning light arises, to the rays of which there is no limit. Thou art the lord of forms, with numerous colors, who conceals himself within his eye to his children. Thou art the mighty enchanter among the cycle of the Gods, thou swift runner, with quick strides. Thou art the mighty God who comes to him who calls for him, who delivers the oppressed from his tortures. Come to my voice. I am the cow. Thy name is in my mouth. I am going to utter it. Hakahaka is thy name. Furaa is thy name. Aakarsa is thy name. Ankrobata is thy name. Khermauserau is thy name. Kharosata is thy name. I adore thy name. I am the cow. Listen to my voice, on the day when thou puttest a flame under the head of Ra. Behold he is in the Tuat, and he is mighty in Heliopolis. Grant that he may be like one who is on earth. He is thy son, who loves thee. Do not ignore his name. Come to Osiris N. Grant that a flame may arise under his head, for he is the soul of the great body which rests in Heliopolis; the shining one, the form of the firstborn is his name. Barokatat'aua is his name. Come, grant him to be like one of thy followers, for he is even as thou art. Said on the image of a cow, made of pure gold, to be put on the neck of the deceased. Also if it is painted on new papyrus, and put under his head, there will be a quantity of flames all around him like those that are on earth. This is a very great protection, which the cow granted to her son Ra, after he had gone to rest. His abode is surrounded by warriors of blazing fire. If thou puttest this Goddess on the neck of the King who is on earth, he is like fire in pursuing his enemies, his horses cannot stop. If thou puttest it on the neck of a man after his death, he is mighty in the Netherworld. Nobody will drive him away from the gates of the Tuat undeviatingly. And thou shall say when thou puttest this Goddess on the neck of the deceased: O Amon of Amons, thou who art in the sky, turn thy face towards the body of thy son, make him sound in the Netherworld. This book is most secret. Do not let it be seen by any man, for it is forbidden to know it. Let it be hidden. It is called the book of the mistress of the hidden abode. This is the end.

Notes:
Chapters 162-165 are of a very late date. They are of a different character from the other chapters of the Book of the Dead. They belong rather to the magic books of the old Egyptians. When they were written, there was a decay in the religion, which drifted more and more into magic, for which the Egyptians were famous under the Roman Empire. We find there a great number of barbarous words unintelligible to us, and probably also to the old scribes, since they differ widely according to the papyri. They remind us of those found in the magical texts. It is probable that Chapter 162 is older than the following; several papyri end with it, and it has the rubric "this is the end," which is found in the older texts after Chapter 149. The late Dr. Pleyte, of Leyden, made a special study of these chapters, and of several others of late date. The collation which he published of various documents is the text on which this translation has been made. The vignette generally consists of a cow, having between her horns a solar disk, with two plumes. Occasionally behind her, there is a Goddess with a cow's head having the same attribute. This cow is considered to be the Goddess Nut, the mother of Ra. An image of the cow, made of pure gold, is to be put on the neck of the deceased; or, what would be much easier and cheaper, it is to be painted on a hypocephalus of new papyrus, and put under the deceased's head. Part of this chapter is the usual text found on the hypocephali. The result of the gift of one of these amulets will be that in the Netherworld the deceased will be surrounded by flames. This is the effect of the presence of the amulets here described. It does not take place in this world, but in the other, where Ra himself enjoys a similar protection, being surrounded by "warriors of blazing fire."This image likely represents the stunning sunsets often seen in Egypt. All translators have interpreted the term as "heat," referring to the body's vital heat. However, the true meaning is "flame," implying a large quantity of flames that will protect the deceased. The lion addressed by the cow, a God of light and fire, is probably Ra himself.

Chapter CLXIII: Preventing a Body from Decaying in the Afterlife

This chapter discusses how to prevent a body from decaying in the afterlife, rescuing it from soul-devouring entities, and protecting it from evil Gods. The deceased can move freely and do as they please without restraint. The soul of the great body in Arohabu protects the body of Hanirta, the lord of motion, who rests in the marshes of Senhakarokana.

The text calls upon the soul of souls to deliver Osiris N. from the God with a terrifying face, who consumes souls with flames from their mouths. The chapter emphasizes the importance of protecting Osiris N. from enemies and restoring his soul to his body.

The chapter also mentions a serpent with two legs and a two-horned disk, symbolizing protection. If this text is read on earth, it protects a person from hidden dangers and evil spirits. The amulet described in the text has protective powers both on earth and in the afterlife.

Chapter CLXIV: Another Chapter

This chapter praises Sekhet, Bast, daughter of Ra, and other deities. It describes their roles in protecting the deceased and ensuring their safe passage in the afterlife. The text emphasizes the power and valor of these deities, who protect the deceased from evil spirits and ensure their well-being in the eternal abode.

The chapter also describes a Mut with three faces, symbolizing protection and power. The deceased wrapped in these bandages will be mighty among the Gods in the Netherworld, never repulsed, and will enjoy eternal life and prosperity.Chapter CLXV: Ensuring the Body Thrives in the Afterlife

This chapter focuses on ensuring the body remains intact and prospers in the afterlife. It calls upon the God Amon, known for his mysterious forms and hidden colors, to protect the deceased. The text emphasizes the importance of knowing Amon's names and forms, which are believed to shield the deceased and grant them eternal rest in the Tuat (the underworld). The chapter also describes specific rituals and amulets that should be used to protect the body from harm and ensure it remains whole and powerful.

Chapter CLXVI: The Pillow

This chapter, often found in tombs, is about awakening and triumphing over suffering. It invokes Ptah, who has defeated the enemies of the deceased, and Horus, whose head was restored after being severed. The text assures that the deceased's head will remain intact and they will be victorious in the afterlife.

Chapter CLXVII: Restoring the Eye

This chapter recounts how Thoth restored the Eye after it was wounded by Ra, calming its fury. It symbolizes the restoration and healing of the deceased, ensuring they are whole and sound.

Chapter CLXVIII: Gods and Genii of the Tuat

This chapter, not originally part of the Book of the Dead, describes various Gods and genii in the Tuat who bestow blessings on the deceased. It includes vignettes of these deities and mentions the libations made by Osiris N., who is now the lord of abundance.

Chapter CLXIX: Raising the Funereal Bed

This chapter describes the deceased as a lion, a sphinx, and Horus, who avenges his father. It speaks of the deceased's journey, their body being nourished and purified, and their soul residing in the sky. The text emphasizes the deceased's strength, purity, and eternal existence, free from judgment and imprisonment.Chapter CLXX: Arranging the Funereal Bed

Your limbs are restored, and your bones are set. The earth protects your flesh. You are like Horus within the egg; when you rise, you see the divine body of Ra and move towards the horizon, to the place you desire. There are cheers and welcomes, with offerings on the altar. Horus lifts you as he did for Osiris in the sacred abode. Hail, Osiris, you are reborn. Anubis on his mountain ensures your bandages grow. Ptah Sokaris allows you to touch the divine house's ornaments. Thoth brings you divine words, guiding you to the sky's horizon where your spirit wishes to be, just as he did for Osiris. Your white diadem is on your brow. Nemu is with you, granting you leadership. Hail, rise on your bed and come forth. Ra lifts you on the horizon in his boat. Hail, you are raised by Imu, granting you eternal endurance. Hail, you are raised by Amsu of Koptos, adored by the shrine's Gods. Hail, blessed be your peaceful arrival at your eternal house and monument. Salutations in Pu Tepu, in the shrine your spirit loves. Your soul is mighty, raised from your resting place, greater than the victim embraced by the Gods. You are like the God who creates beings, more admirable than the Gods. Your splendor surpasses the Glorified, your spirits are mightier. Hail, you are raised by Ptah Anebefres, placing your dwelling before the Gods. Hail, you are Horus, son of Osiris, created by Nut. You shine like Ra on the horizon, lighting the earth with your rays. The Gods invite you to see your eternal house. Rennut, the great one, who conceived Tmu, raises you. I am the second outcome of the sky, the third of the light-maker. I emerged from the womb, an infant like my father, with no perverse actions in my life.

Chapter CLXXI: Wrapping the Deceased in a Pure Garment

O Tmu, Shu, Tefnut, Seb, Nut, Osiris, Isis, Sut, Nephthys, Horus of the two Horizons, Hathor in the great dwelling, Chepera, Mentu lord of Thebes, Amon lord of Nestaui, great and small cycles of Gods, Gods and Goddesses from Nu, Sebek of Shet, Sebek in all his names and abodes, Gods of the South and North, Gods in heaven and on earth, grant a pure garment to the mighty Chu N. Make him glorious and remove all wrongs. This pure garment is his forever, for eternity, cleansing all wrongs.

Chapter CLXXII: Reciting Ceremonies in the Netherworld

With incense, I inhale the smell of natron and incense, purified by sacred utterances from my mouth. I am pure, like the fishes in the river, towards the statue in the house of purification. The words of N. are pure. Blessed be you, N., pleasing to Ptah, Anebefres, all Gods, and Goddesses. Your beauty is like a calm stream, like the finest water, like a festival hall where everyone...Chapter CLXX: Arranging the Funereal Bed

Chapter CLXXI: Wrapping the Deceased in a Pure Garment

O Tmu, Shu, Tefnut, Seb, Nut, Osiris, Isis, Sut, Nephthys, Horus of the two Horizons, Hathor in the great dwelling, Chepera, Mentu lord of Thebes, Amon lord of Nestaui, great and small cycles of Gods, Gods and Goddesses from Nu, Sebek of Shet, Sebek in all his names and abodes, Gods of the South and North, Gods in heaven and on earth, grant a pure garment to the mighty Chu N. Make him glorious and remove all wrongs. This pure garment is his forever, for eternity, cleansing all wrongs.

Chapter CLXXII: Reciting Ceremonies in the Netherworld

With incense, I inhale the smell of natron and incense, purified by sacred utterances from my mouth. I am pure, like the fishes in the river, towards the statue in the house of purification. The words of N. are pure. Blessed be you, N., pleasing to Ptah, Anebefres, all Gods, and Goddesses. Your beauty is like a calm stream, like the finest water, like a festival hall where everyone...

Your beauty is like the pillars of Ptah, like the shoots of the maut plant of Ra. N. is the pillar of Ptah and the ewer of Anebefres. O you who are called aloud, you who are called aloud, you the lamented, you are glorified, you are exalted, you are glorious, you are strong. O you who are raised up, you are raised up, N. has been raised up by means of all the manifold ceremonies done to him; your enemies are struck down; Ptah has struck down your enemies, you are victorious and you have dominion over them. Your words are listened to, what you have ordered is done, you are raised, you are triumphant before the Circles of Gods attached to every God and every Goddess. O you who are called aloud, second verse. Your head is woven by a woman from Asia; your face shines brighter than the moon; the top of your head is lapis blue; your hair is darker than the doors of the Tuat, your hair is black like the night; your forehead is adorned with blue; the rays of Horus are on your face. Your garments are of gold; Horus has decked them with blue; your eyebrows, the two sisters joined together; Horus has adorned them with blue; your nose inhales the perfume and your nostrils are like the winds in the sky. Your eyes are the seers of the hill of Bachau, your upper eyelids are enduring forever; their lashes are of real lapis; your pupils are pleasant gifts, and your lower eyelids are painted with antimony. Your lips utter for you words of truth, they repeat the words of truth of Ra which are well pleasing to the Gods. Your teeth are the two heads of the serpent by which the two Gods are seized, your tongue is voluble; your voice is more shrill than that of the bird in the marshes; your ears are well established at their place, they go with you to the land of Amenta. O you who are called aloud, third verse. Your neck is adorned with gold, it is girt with electron; your throat and your lungs are like Anubis; your backbone is like the Uat' Goddesses; your back is lined with gold and girt with electron; your loins are like Nephthys, a Nile which is flowing. Your buttocks are two eggs of crystal, your legs are well fastened for walking, you are sitting in your place you have received from the Gods your two eyes. O you who are called aloud, fourth verse. Your throat is like Anubis, your limbs are necklaces made of gold; your breasts are two eggs of crystal which Horus has painted blue, your forearms are adorned with topaz, your shoulders are well established on their base; your heart is happy every day, your whole heart is the work of the two divine Powers, your body worships the stars of the Gods above and below; for your belly is like a calm sky, and your bowels are the Tuat which nobody can fathom, and which sends out light in the dark night; its offerings are eatable plants. He (N.) praises the Majesty of Thoth, saying: the desires of his beautiful person take place in my tomb; as my God commanded me. Every pure thing he loves is there. O you who are called aloud, fifth verse. Your thighs are a pond in a time of abundant inundation; a pond which is lined by the children of the God of water; your legs which go to and fro are of gold; your knees are lentisks in the marshes; your feet are firm every day; your shin-bones lead you on the right path. Your arms are pillars on their bases; your fingers are of gold; their nails are like knives of flint in what they do for you. O you who are called aloud, sixth verse. You put on the pure garment and you divest your apron when you stretch yourself on the funereal bed; haunches are cut for your Aa, and a heart is offered unto your mummy. You receive a bandage of the finest linen from the hands of the attendant of Ra; you eat on your resting couch bread which has been baked by the fire Goddess herself; you eat the haunch, you seize the meat which has been prepared by Ra in his holy place; you wash your feet in silver basins made by the skillful artist Sokaris; you eat bread placed on the altar, and prepared by the holy fathers, you live upon baked cakes and hot drinks from the store-house; you inhale the smell of flowers; your heart is not reluctant at the sight of offerings; your ministrants make for you the loaves and the cakes of the Powers of Heliopolis; and they themselves bring you the sacred things; your offerings have been chosen for you; and your ordinances are in the gates of the Great Dwelling; you rise like Sahu and you arrive like the morning star; Nut stretches forth her arms towards you; Sahu, the son of Ra, and Nut, the mother of the Gods, the two great Gods of the sky, they speak one to another saying: Take him in your arms; I have brought in my arms the form of N. in the happy day when he is glorified, when his memory is recorded, when he is in the mouth of all generations. You, raised one, you hear how you are glorified throughout all your house. O you who are called aloud, seventh verse. Anubis has given him his shroud; he has done all that pleased him; the high-priest has prepared his ribbon; for he is the provider of the great God; you go and wash yourself in the lake of Perfection, you make offerings in the house of the Gods of the sky, and you propitiate the lord of Heliopolis; you receive the water of Ra in ewers, and milk in large vases. O you raised one, you make offerings on the altar, and you wash your feet upon the stone of, on the banks of the divine lake; you come forth and you see Ra upon the four pillars which are the arms of the sky; on the head of Anmutef, and on the arms of Apuat who opens for you the path; you see the horizon where are all the sacred things which you desire. O you who are called aloud, eighth verse. All the good things have been spread out for you, before Ra. You have a beginning and you have an end as Horus and Thoth have ordered for you. They call upon N., they see how he is glorious, they give him to come forth like a God to meet the Powers of Heliopolis. You journey on the great path as your mummy has received the sacred things from your father; your hands are wrapped in linen every day; the beginning of the journey of the God is at the gate of the Great Dwelling, O you who are called aloud, ninth verse. N. breathes the air for his nose and for his nostrils, he receives a thousand geese and sixty baskets of all things good and pure; your enemies have been struck down; they are no more."I have anointed you with holy oil. I have brought you the offering that destroys your face. (2) Notes: This chapter is also found in London 9900. The vignette at the end shows Osiris sitting in a shrine. Before him are offerings of fowl and cattle presented by Horus to his father. At the beginning, the deceased is seen with raised arms, symbolizing Horus, with the following words above him: 'Adoration to Osiris, Khenta Amenta, the great God, the lord of Abydos, king forever, prince of eternity, the venerable God in Restau, pronounced by N. I give you grain, lord of the Gods, the one God who lives on justice. I am your son Horus. I have come to you. I avenge you, I bring you Maat, to the place where the circle of your Gods is. Grant me to be among your followers and to smite your enemies. I have established your food offerings on the earth forever.' The full version from the Ritual at Abydos reads: 'I have anointed your head with the oil of Horus' brow; if it is destroyed there (on his brow), he is destroyed as a God; i.e., his divinity is destroyed.' 

Chapter CLXXIV: Chapter of causing the Chii to come out of the great door in the sky. It is read (1) to you by your son (Horus). The great ones tremble when they see the sword in your hand as you emerge from the Tuat. Hail to you, the wise one, created by Seb, born of Nut. The cycles of the Gods are at rest. Horus rests in his dwelling (2), Tum rests in his abode (?). All the Gods of East and West rest in the great Goddess (3) of birth, between the arms of her who gave birth to the God. When I am born, I see and recognize where I am. I have been raised in my place. The order has been accomplished by her who hates sleep and depression, and who stands in Utenet. My bread comes from Pu, and I receive my form in Heliopolis. Horus, following the command from his father, the lord of clouds, Astes, raised him, and I have been raised by Tmu. I am the great one. I come forth between the legs of the cycle of the Gods. I have been conceived by Sechet, and Shestet (4) gave me birth to be her star, Sothis, the first one, the great walker who brings Ra through the sky every day. I have come to my abode. I have united the two diadems. I shine like a star. O ye flowers, the name of which is 'the precious bunch,' I am the lotus that comes out of the holy earth; when I am plucked, I settle myself at the nostrils of the Great Figure. I have come out of the lake of flame, I have received justice instead of evil. I am near the white cloth (5), and I keep watch over the Urrei in the night of the great flood of tears. (6) I shine like Nefertmu, the lotus at the nostril of Ra when he comes forth on the horizon every day, and the Gods are purified by his sight. N. is triumphant among the ka, smiting the hearts through his great wisdom. He is near the God, he is the Sau (7) (the knowing one) at the western (right) side of Ra. I have come to my abode among the ka, uniting the hearts through my great wisdom. I am Sau near the God, at the western side of Ra; my sceptre (?) is in my hand. I am called the great favorite, as I am clad in red garments. I am Sau, on the western side of Ra, with a stout heart in the cave of Nu. Notes: This chapter is already found in the pyramid of Unas (1. 379-399). Prof. Erman (Zeitschr., XXXIII, p. 2) has made a special study of it and pointed out that the title of this chapter originates from a misunderstanding of the word o M, which should be a star and not a gate or a door. Were it not for the vignette, which shows the deceased, the woman Muthotepet, coming out of a door, we would translate: 'Chapter of the coming forth of the Chu as a great star in the sky,' in accordance with these words found in the chapter: 'Shestet gave me birth to be her star, Sothis,' etc. Only two papyri contain this chapter, one in London and one in Paris. The London text has a vignette with these words: 'the coming out of the door in the sky by ...' 1. M. Maspero translates: 'your son has made (the sacrifice).' The word is used here as in the rubric of Chapter 141, 'to say, to speak.' This speech is a ceremonial act, one of the v\\ done for the deceased. 2. We noticed before (Chapter 160, note 2) that is a variant for when applying to Tmu. Here it applies to Horus. The unknown word [ [ [ being parallel, I give it conjecturally a similar sense. 3. 'the great one, the great Goddess,' and its variants occur frequently in the Book of the Dead and seem to be a name of the sky. 4. which is found in the papyrus, is clearly a mistake for the name of the Goddess Shestet, which we read in the text of Unas. 5. Perhaps a tent in which he will shelter the Ursei. 6. See note 1, Chapter 4, and Z//^ IVor/i, Vol. III, p. 46. I suppose it means here a heavy rain. 7. In the pictures in the royal tombs, the sun-God stands in his boat between and . Here it is said that Sau is at the West of Ra, meaning on his right side. Ra is spoken of here as if he were a human being, turning towards the South as all Egyptians did. His west is his right-hand side. Even now, the Egyptian fellaheen in their language do not often say right and left; they generally use the points of the compass: west of you, etc.

Chapter CLXXV: Chapter of not dying a second death in the Netherworld. O Thoth (1)! What has become of the children of Nut? They have stirred up hostilities, raised storms, committed iniquity, raised rebellion, perpetrated murder, and done oppression. The strong have acted against the weak in all they have done to me. Grant, O Thoth, what Tmu has decreed. You do not see the iniquities, you are not pained by their attacks on the years and their invasions on the months, because they have done their mischiefs in secret. I am your pallet, O Thoth, and I bring you your inkstand; I am not one of those who do mischief in secret. Let no mischief be done to me. O Tmu! What is this place to which I have journeyed? It is without water and without air! It is all abyss, utter darkness, sheer perplexity. One lives here in peace of heart. There is no pleasure of love here. Let there be granted to me glory instead of water, air, and pleasures of love; and peace of heart instead of bread and beer. [Decree this, Tmu, that if I see your face, I shall not be pained by your sufferings (2). Tmu decrees; behold, the great Gods have given him this mission, he will reign on his throne, and he will inherit his throne in the Isle of Fire: and for you, I decree that the God may see him as his second self, and that my face may see your face. My lord Tmu, what is the duration of my life? You are for eternities of eternities, the duration of endless years; and behold, I am going to deface all I have done: this earth will become water, an inundation as it was in the beginning. I will remain with Osiris, and I will make my form like another serpent, whom no man will know, and no God will see. It is good what I have done to Osiris, who is exalted above all the Gods. I have given him power in the region of the Netherworld, and his son Horus will inherit his throne in the Isle of Fire. I will make his throne in the boat of millions of years. Horus is well established on his seat to take possession of his place of rest; also, I send a soul to Sut in the West, who is exalted above all Gods; and I have caused his soul to be guarded in the boat, so that he may feel reverential fear of the divine body (Osiris).] O my father Osiris! I have done for you what your father Ra did for you. Let me have increase upon earth, let me keep my dwelling place, let my heir be vigorous, let my sepulchre flourish, and my dependents upon earth. Let all my adversaries be crushed to pieces with Selk'et (the scorpion Goddess) over their ruin. I am your son, O my father Ra! You have been the cause of this Life, Health, and Strength. Horus is established upon his throne. Grant that my duration of life may be that of one who attains beatitude. (3) Notes: The translation and notes of this chapter, except what is in brackets, are Renouf's work. They are taken from the introduction he published to his edition of the papyrus of Ani (p. 16). The vignette shows the deceased and his wife worshipping Thoth. This chapter is found in the papyrus of Ani and at greater length in a papyrus of the Museum of Leyden, from which it has been copied by Naville into his edition. The Leyden text is unfortunately very incomplete, both in the upper and lower parts of the columns. The two texts differ materially in some of their readings and will require considerable study before a satisfactory translation can be given. 1. The deceased is evidently supposed to be just arrived in a place of utter darkness and desolation and expresses his feelings of distress to Thoth in the opening address. 2. The text of Leyden is much more complete. Owing probably to want of space, the scribe of Ani has shortened his text. There the omissions are so considerable that it is impossible to find a sense. I have often adopted the reading of the Leyden papyrus in the translation of this part of the chapter. 3. The remaining columns in the Leyden text are unfortunately incomplete."The manuscript, although incomplete, shows that the deceased is reborn as Osiris through his son Horus. There is a cry of adoration to him in Sutenhenen, and joy in En-aaref. The Gods are pleased to see him inherit his throne and rule the earth. Sut is terrified by the transformation. All generations of mankind, past, present, and future, show respect. The chapter mentions the "Hoeing" and the bloodshed in Sutenhenen, referencing the myth of mankind's destruction, and other details about Osiris. This chapter is recited over an image of Horus made of lapis lazuli placed at the deceased's throat and also in the Netherworld.

Chapter CLXXVI: Not dying a second time in the Netherworld. I reject the land of the East. I avoid the dungeon because I haven't committed the forbidden acts. I have passed through the purification place in Meskat; the inviolate God has given me his glorious attributes on the day the two Earths united before the Master of all things. Knowing this chapter makes one powerful in the Netherworld.

Chapter CLXXVII: Raising the Chu and vivifying his soul in the Netherworld. O Nut, who created the father from his earth and Horus after him, who bound his wings like a hawk and perfected his words, who showed him his abode among the stars. He is the great star of Nut. You see N. speaking to the Glorified, for he is the great form who will not rule if you are not among them. You see N.'s head as a ba (ram); his horns are like those of a sacrificed black ram. Horus with blue eyes guards Horus with red eyes in his sickness and wrath. Let his soul not be opposed, let his messengers come to him quickly. The God says: your words are those of the father of the Gods, your name will be triumphant before the Gods; they exalt you and the cycle of the Gods give you their hands. The God tells the father of the Gods: take possession of the door of the ka on the horizon, let them open their gates; you are welcome, prevail over them, let them advance towards the God. When they come out, they raise their faces and see him before the great God Amsu. Your head will not perish, and what you have done before men and Gods will not be destroyed.

Chapter CLXXVIII: Raising the body, giving it eyes, ears, and fixing its head. You have received the eye of Horus; your table is a table of offerings. Hail, Hunnu, purify your body; they have eaten the eye of Horus, the olive of Heliopolis, and destroy what is wrong in Osiris's body. N.'s mouth was thirsty, but he will never hunger or thirst again; Chas delivers him from hunger. O you who fill the vases, chiefs who distribute bread and cakes, and manage the waterflood; Ra ordered bread and beer for N. They seize the gifts and give him wheat, barley, and loaves, for he is the great bull. Grant N. the charge of the five loaves in the funerary chapel; three in heaven for Ra, two on earth for the Gods, and Nu sees them. O Ra, be gracious to N. on this happy day when N. joined Shu and Isis. They give bread and beer to N. and do all good and pure things on this happy day, bringing him the eye of Horus whenever he arrives to see the God. You take possession of water and march towards the altar of Sashert: four measures of water, as commanded by Osiris to N. Shu has handed over his wealth to N.; they are your bread and beer. Awake, lofty judge; awake, sleeper; your offerings are brought before Thoth and Horus, who comes from the Nile, and Apuat from Asert. N.'s mouth is pure, and his tongue in his mouth, for N. hates filth and is washed from impurity like Sut in the city of Rehui. Feed N. with you; let him eat, drink, sit, and be mighty as you are. Navigate as you navigate. N.'s tent is woven in the field of Aarru, his running water is in the Garden of Hotepit. Offerings are made to him among the Gods; N.'s drink is the wine of Ra. He goes around the sky like Ra, travels over the sky like Thoth. N. rejects hunger and thirst. N. has received bread from the lord of eternity. He ordered that N. be conceived at night and born in the morning, close to Ra's follower, before the morning star. N. was conceived and born of N., bringing you the loaves found in the eye of Horus, on the tennu tree bough. When he came, Khenta Amenta brought him the victuals and offerings of Horus in his abodes. N. lives of them; as Horus drinks, N. drinks; his food is on the altar of Sashert. N. is welcome to Anubis on his mountain. Hail, N., your figure is as it was on earth, living and renewed every day. Your face is unveiled, and you see the lord of the horizon; he gives bread to N. at his hour of the day and at his appointed time in the night. Horus has avenged you. He has smashed the jawbones of your enemies and smitten the violent one at the door of his fortress. Hail, N., your enemies are no more, the scales are right concerning you in the great hall, you make long strides like Osiris, the lord of arrivals in Amenta. He arrives when he likes, sees the great God in his creations, and life is given to his nostrils. He is triumphant over his enemies. Hail, N. You hate falsehood, propitiate the lord of all things in the night of "stopping the tears," and receive sweet life from the mouth of the Gods. Thoth is satisfied in giving you victory over your enemies. Nut spreads her wings over you in her name of the veil of the sky, giving you to follow the great God, and your enemies are no more. She delivers you from all evil in her name of Chnumeturit, for she is the great one among her children. O chief of the hours, in front of Ra, make way for N. to arrive in the circle of Osiris, the living lord of the two earths, who lives eternally. N. follows Nefertmu, he is the lotus at Ra's nostrils, pure in the presence of the Gods; he sees Ra eternally.

Chapter CLXXIX: Coming forth when going out of yesterday and coming in the present day, equipped by one's own hands. I am raised from yesterday, I come today, I co...Chapter CLXXIX: Emerging from the past and entering the present, empowered by one's own actions. I rise from yesterday and step into today. I am the essence flowing from the tree, the life force emerging from its form. I stand before the lord of the white crown, gracious and confident. My words are firm before the lord of the red crown, who restores his eye. Though I died yesterday, I am reborn today. I approach the doorkeeper of the great God, emerging victorious against my enemy. He is delivered to me, unable to escape my grasp, diminishing in my possession before the great circle of Gods in the Netherworld. I wear the diadem of the great Goddess, symbolizing my authority among the living Gods. My enemy is subdued, unable to escape, dwindling in my possession before the Gods of Osiris during his festival. I am the master of the sword, and it will not be taken from me. I rest in the garden of Hotepit, as commanded by the lords of Cheraba, standing tall among the mighty. I am strong, resting in the isles of the garden of Aarru.

Chapter CLXXX: Emerging by day, praising Ra in the Amenta, honoring the inhabitants of the Tuat, and opening the way for the mighty soul in the Netherworld. Ra sets as Osiris, resplendent among the Glorified and the Gods of the Amenta. He is the one, the marvelous in the Tuat, the exalted soul in the Netherworld, Unneferu, eternal and everlasting. Hail to you in the Tuat, where your son Horus rests within you. You speak to him, granting him radiance before the inhabitants of the Tuat, making him the great star. He brings his essence to the Tuat, traveling within it as the son of Ra, born from Tmu. Hail to you in the Tuat, God seated on your throne, holding your scepter, king of the Tuat, and lord of Acherta. Great prince wearing the double diadem, great God who conceals his dwelling, lord of wisdom, chief of his circle of Gods. Hail to you in the Tuat, praises to all within you. The weeping Gods honor you, clapping their hands, imploring, and praying before you. Your soul rejoices, and your body is glorious, exalted in the Amenta. The powers praise you within the bounds of the Tuat, Teb Temt resting in his covering. Hail, Osiris, I am your temple servant, dwelling in your divine abode. You speak to me, granting me radiance before the inhabitants of the Tuat, like the great star who brings his essence to the Tuat, traveling within it as the son of Ra, born from Tmu. I rest in the Tuat, master of the dusk, entering and exiting freely. The arms of Tatunen receive me, the blessed lift me up. Stretch your arms towards me, for I know your gates. Guide me, praise me, rejoice in me as in Ra, for I have placed offerings before you, and you take possession of your sustenance as Ra commanded. I am his favorite, his heir on earth. I have arrived. Blessed ones, grant me entry to the Tuat, open the entrance to the good Amenta. I have presented the sceptre to saJm, and the ne/iu/ies to him whose name is hidden. Look at me, blessed ones, divine guides in the Tuat. Grant me your glory, that I may shine like the God of mysteries. Deliver me from the Gods of the pillory, who bind to their posts. Do not bind me, do not send me to the place of destruction. I am the heir of Osiris, receiving the nemines in the Tuat. Look at me, I shine like one of you, becoming like him who praises his father and extols him. Look at me, rejoice in me, grant me exaltation, that I may become like him who destroys his forms. Open the way for my soul, set me on your pedestals. Grant me rest in the good Amenta, show me my dwelling among you, open your ways, unfasten the bolts. O Ra, who guides this earth, guiding the powers and following the course of the Gods. I am the guardian of his door, towing the navigating Gods. I am the only one, the guardian of his door, placing the Gods in their abodes. I am on my pedestal in the Tuat, a possessor among possessors, at the far end of the Tuat. I am blessed in the Acherta, making my resting place in the Amenta, among the powers and Gods. I am Ra's favorite, the mysterious Bennu entering and exiting the Tuat in peace. I am the lord of the thrones above, traversing the horizon with Ra. My offerings are in the sky in the field of Ra, and my portion on earth in the garden of Aarru. I journey in the Tuat like Ra, weighing words like Thoth, marching as I will, hastening like Sahu the mysterious one, born as the two Gods. I am the chief bearer of offerings to the Gods of the Tuat, giving offerings to the Glorified. I am the brave one who strikes his enemies. O Gods, O Glorified who precede Ra, escorting his soul, tow me as you tow him, guiding me as you guide Ra and those in the sky. I am the lofty power in the Amenta.

Chapter CLXXXI: Arriving before the Divine circle of Osiris and the Gods, the guides in the Tuat, the guards of their halls, the heralds of their gates, and the doorkeepers of their pylons in the Amenta. Taking the form of a living soul and praising Osiris, the lord of his circle of Gods. Hail to you, Chenta Amenta, Unneferu, lord of Tatsert. You shine like Ra, who comes to see you, rejoicing in your beauty. His disk is your disk, his rays are your rays, his diadem is your diadem, his height is your height, his splendor is your splendor, his beauty is your beauty, his might is your might, his scent is your scent. His width is your width, his abode is your abode, his throne is your throne, his lineage is your lineage, his judgment is your judgment, his Ament is your Ament, his wealth is your wealth, his duration is your duration, his creations are your creations. As he is, so are you. As you are, so is he. He shall not die, and neither will you. If he does not triumph over his enemies, neither will you. No evil will befall him, and none will befall you, forever and ever. Hail, Osiris, son of Nut, lord of horns, wearing the high atef crown, to whom the diadem and the hik scepter have been given in the presence of the cycle of the Gods. Turn has instilled fear of his might in the hearts of mankind, Gods, the Glorified, and the dead. Royal power has been granted to him in Heliopolis. He is the great one.Osiris, the lord of fear in his two abodes, is revered in Restau and celebrated in Abydos. He triumphs before all Gods, his power felt across the earth. The great ones stand before him, the prince of the Gods of the Tuat, the mighty sky lord, and king of the living and the dead. Thousands glorify him in Cheraba, and the future ones rejoice in him. He receives the best offerings in Memphis, and his festival is celebrated in Sechem. Horus, his son, avenges him, restoring his body and joining his bones. Osiris rises, protected by the Gods, with Nut and his sisters, Isis and Nephthys, filling him with life and strength. The Gods gather good things for him, praising him forever. Osiris shines brilliantly, powerful and glorified, like Anubis. Ra rejoices in his beauty, and Seb grants his desires in the Amenta. Osiris navigates the sky daily, leading Ra to Nut, living in the Amenta. He is with Horus, protected by Ra and Thoth, with Isis's health within him. 

I come to you, Osiris, lord of Ta-tsert, eternal Unneferu. My heart is pure, and I bring offerings to you. I have struck down your enemies and purified myself for your festival. I have prepared offerings for your soul and the Gods who follow you. Knowing this book protects one from evil, granting entry to the Tuat and receiving good things before its inhabitants.

Chapter CLXXXII: Thoth, the perfect scribe, repels Osiris's enemies, ensuring the morning light shines on him daily. Thoth, the lord of laws, dispels darkness and gives Osiris the breath of life. He ensures Ra and Osiris set and rise together, reviving Osiris's heart. Thoth, the great magician, pacifies the two earths and gives life to the future ones. Osiris triumphs over his enemies, protected by Thoth's amulet. Thoth, the high God, opens the good roads and praises Osiris Unneferu, eternal and everlasting.

Chapter CLXXXIII: Adoration to Osiris, praising Unneferu, and exalting the lord of Ta-tsert. Thoth brings sweet breezes and the breath of life to Osiris, illuminating his path and removing wrongs. He appeases the Gods and makes the two earths peaceful. Horus, Osiris's son, triumphs before all Gods, receiving royal power and dominion over the earth. The throne of Seb and the high dignity of Tmu are his. Osiris joins the firmament, bringing forth growth on mountains and earth. He hands over all Gods to Horus, who commands them at his gates.Osiris, the lord of fear in his two abodes, is revered in Restau and celebrated in Abydos. He triumphs before all Gods, his power felt across the earth. The great ones stand before him, the prince of the Gods of the Tuat, the mighty sky lord, and king of the living and the dead. Thousands glorify him in Cheraba, and the future ones rejoice in him. He receives the best offerings in Memphis, and his festival is celebrated in Sechem. Horus, his son, avenges him, restoring his body and joining his bones. Osiris rises, protected by the Gods, with Nut and his sisters, Isis and Nephthys, filling him with life and strength. The Gods gather good things for him, praising him forever. Osiris shines brilliantly, powerful and glorified, like Anubis. Ra rejoices in his beauty, and Seb grants his desires in the Amenta. Osiris navigates the sky daily, leading Ra to Nut, living in the Amenta. He is with Horus, protected by Ra and Thoth, with Isis's health within him.

I come to you, Osiris, lord of Ta-tsert, eternal Unneferu. My heart is pure, and I bring offerings to you. I have struck down your enemies and purified myself for your festival. I have prepared offerings for your soul and the Gods who follow you. Knowing this book protects one from evil, granting entry to the Tuat and receiving good things before its inhabitants.

Chapter CLXXXII: Thoth, the perfect scribe, repels Osiris's enemies, ensuring the morning light shines on him daily. Thoth, the lord of laws, dispels darkness and gives Osiris the breath of life. He ensures Ra and Osiris set and rise together, reviving Osiris's heart. Thoth, the great magician, pacifies the two earths and gives life to the future ones. Osiris triumphs over his enemies, protected by Thoth's amulet. Thoth, the high God, opens the good roads and praises Osiris Unneferu, eternal and everlasting.

Chapter CLXXXIII: Adoration to Osiris, praising Unneferu, and exalting the lord of Ta-tsert. Thoth brings sweet breezes and the breath of life to Osiris, illuminating his path and removing wrongs. He appeases the Gods and makes the two earths peaceful. Horus, Osiris's son, triumphs before all Gods, receiving royal power and dominion over the earth. The throne of Seb and the high dignity of Tmu are his. Osiris joins the firmament, bringing forth growth on mountains and earth. He hands over all Gods to Horus, who commands them at his gates.

He has commanded, and they fulfill it at once; your heart is satisfied, lord of the Gods, and overjoyed. Egypt and the desert are at peace; they are the vassals of your royal diadem. The temples and cities are well-ordered; they bring you tributes and make libations to your name forever. You are called upon, and your name is praised; your ka is gratified by funerary meals. The Glorified who follow you sprinkle water on your food beside the dead souls in this land. All your thoughts are excellent like those of the one who was at the beginning. Be crowned, son of Nut, as the Inviolate God is crowned; you are living, revived, renewed, and perfect. Your father Ra gives health to all your limbs, and your divine circle praises you. Isis is with you, she will never leave you until all your enemies are struck down. All lands praise your beauties like Ra when he rises every morning; you are crowned like him who is high on his pedestal, your beauties are exalted, your strides lengthened. You have received the royal power of Seb, your father who creates your beauties; your mother gave existence to your limbs, Nut who bore the Gods bore you to be the chief of the five Gods. The white crown of the South is placed on your head; you seize the hook and the flail. When you were still in the womb, before you appeared on earth, you were crowned to be lord of the two earths, the crown of Ra was on your head. The Gods come to you, bowing down, the fear of you possesses them; they see you with the might of Ra, and the valor of your majesty fills their hearts. Life is with you, abundance is attached to you. I offer Maat before you: grant that I may be in the train of your majesty like one who is on the earth. May your name be called upon, may it be found among the just ones. I have come to the city of this God, to the city of God, to the region of old time; my soul, my heart, my spirit are in this land. The God of it is the lord of justice, the lord of abundance, the great and venerable one, who is towed through the whole earth; he journeys to the South in his boat, and to the North driven by the winds, and his oars, to be entertained with gifts according to the command of the God, the lord of peace therein, who left me free of care. The God therein rejoices in him who practices justice; he grants an old age to him who has done so; he is beloved, and the end of it is a good burial and a sepulture in Ta-tsert. I have come to you: my hands bring Maat, my heart does not contain any falsehood, I offer you Maat before your face, I know her; I swear by her: I have done no evil thing on earth; I have never wronged a man of his property. I am Thoth, the perfect and pure writer: my hands are pure. I have put away all evil things: I write justice and I hate evil: for I am the writing-reed of the Inviolate God, who utters his words, and whose words are written in the two earths. I am Thoth, the lord of justice, who gives victory to him who is injured and who takes the defense of the oppressed, of him who is wronged in his property. I have dispelled darkness; I have driven away the storm; I have given air to Unneferu, and the sweet breezes of the North when he comes out of the womb of his mother. I have given him to enter into the mysterious cave where the heart of the God whose heart is motionless is revived, Unneferu, the son of Nut, the victorious.

Note: This hymn is taken from the papyrus of Unneferu, in London. See note 1 in Chapter 1.

Chapter CLXXXV: Giving praise to Osiris, falling on the earth before the lord of eternity; propitiating the God with what he loves, speaking the truth, the lord of which is not known. Hail to you, venerable God, great and beneficent prince of eternity, in his abode in the Sektit boat. Acclamations are given to him in the sky and on earth; he is exalted by the past and present. Great is the fear he inspires in the hearts of men, of the Glorified and of the dead. His soul was given to him in Tattu, his might in Heracleopolis, his image in Heliopolis, and his power over forms in the double sanctuary. I have come to you; my heart holds right, my heart contains no falsehood. Give me to be among the living, to navigate up and down in your train.

Chapter CLXXXVI: Adoration to Hathor, the lady of the West, falling down before Mehurit. I have come to you, to see your beauties, give me to be at the head of your followers and among your divine attendants. Many papyri end with a picture representing Hathor of the West, in the company of the Goddess Thueris coming out of the mountain where the burial is to take place. The text, which is generally very corrupt, as if the writer had neglected the words for the picture, is an adoration to Hathor, which varies in its form. The text here translated is taken from a papyrus at Leyden.
